Page 1
Afghanistan 
Coordinates: [URL: "https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Afghanistan&params=34_31_N_69_11_E_region:AF_source:geonames_type:city"] 34°31′N 69°11′E
Afghanistan,[c] officially the Islamic Emirate of
Afghanistan,[d] is a landlocked country located at the
crossroads of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Asia"] Central and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Asia"] South Asia. Referred to as the
 Heart of Asia,[22] it is bordered by Pakistan to the east
and south,[e] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran"] Iran to the west, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkmenistan"] Turkmenistan to the
northwest, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uzbekistan"] Uzbekistan to the north, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tajikistan"] Tajikistan to the
northeast, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China"] China to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghanistan%E2%80%93China_border"] northeast and east.
Occupying 652,864 square kilometers (252,072 sq mi)
of land, the country is predominately mountainous with
plains [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghan_Turkestan"] in the north and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sistan_Basin"] the southwest, which are
separated by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindu_Kush"] Hindu Kush mountain range. As of
2021, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demographics_of_Afghanistan"] its population is 40.2 million,[7] composed mostly
of ethnic Pashtuns, Tajiks, Hazaras, and Uzbeks. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kabul"] Kabul
is the country's largest city and serves as its capital.
 Human habitation in Afghanistan dates back to the
 Middle Paleolithic era, and the country's strategic
location along the historic [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silk_Road"] Silk Road has led it to being
described, picturesquely, as the ‘roundabout of the
 ancient world’.[23] Known as the Graveyard of
Empires,[24] the land has historically been home to
 various peoples and has witnessed numerous military
campaigns, including those by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_the_Great"] Alexander the Great, the
 Maurya Empire, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_conquests_of_Afghanistan"] Arab Muslims, the Mongols, the
 British, the Soviet Union, and most recently by an
American-led coalition. Afghanistan also served as the
source from which the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greco-Bactrian_Kingdom"] Greco-Bactrians and the
Mughals, among others, rose to form major empires.[25]
The various conquests and periods in both the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greater_Iran"] Iranian
and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greater_India"] Indian cultural spheres[26][27] made the area a
center for Zoroastrianism, Buddhism, Hinduism, and
later Islam throughout history.[28]
The modern state of Afghanistan began with the
 Durrani dynasty in the 18th century, with the Durrani
Afghan Empire being formed by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmad_Shah_Durrani"] Ahmad Shah Durrani.
The Durrani Empire led conquests in which, at its peak,
encompassed land that spanned from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Iran"] eastern Iran to
 northern India.[29][30] Following its decline and the
death of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmad_Shah_Durrani"] Ahmad Shah Durrani, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timur_Shah_Durrani"] Timur Shah, it was
divided into multiple smaller independent kingdoms,
including but not limited to: Herat, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Principality_of_Qandahar"] Kandahar and
Kabul. Afghanistan would be reunited in the 19th
 century after wars of unification led by Dost
Mohammad Khan, where he conquered the 
Islamic Emirate of Afghanistan

"[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/This_is_the_Home_of_the_Brave"] This is the Home of the Brave"[2]
Status  [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UN_member_state"] UN member state
under an
Page 2
independent principalities in Afghanistan. Dost
 Mohammad died in 1863, weeks after his last campaign
 to unite Afghanistan, and as a result, threw Afghanistan
back into civil war with his successors. During this
 time, Afghanistan became a buffer state in the Great
 Game between the British Empire (in British-ruled
India) and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Empire"] Russian Empire. From India, the British
attempted to subjugate Afghanistan but were repelled in
 the First Anglo-Afghan War. However, the Second
Anglo-Afghan War saw a British victory and the
successful establishment of British political influence
 over Afghanistan. Following the Third Anglo-Afghan
War in 1919, Afghanistan became free of foreign
dominance, and eventually emerged as the independent
 Kingdom of Afghanistan in June 1926 under
 Amanullah Khan. This monarchy lasted almost 50
years, until [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammed_Zahir_Shah"] Zahir Shah was [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1973_Afghan_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat"] overthrown in 1973,
following which the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republic_of_Afghanistan_(1973%E2%80%931978)"] Republic of Afghanistan was
established. Since the late 1970s, Afghanistan's history
has been dominated by extensive warfare, including
 coups, revolutions, invasions, insurgencies, and civil
wars. Due to the effects of war, the country has dealt
 with high levels of terrorism, poverty, and child
malnutrition. Afghanistan's economy is the world's
96th-largest, with a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gross_domestic_product"] gross domestic product (GDP) of
$72.9 billion by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity"] purchasing power parity; the country
fares much worse in terms of per-capita GDP (PPP),
ranking 169th out of 186 countriesas of 2018.
 On 15 August 2021, the country was captured by the
Taliban, which marked the end of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%932021)"] 2001–2021 war,
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_the_lengths_of_United_States_participation_in_wars"] longest war in US history.[31] This led to the
overthrowing of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Republic_of_Afghanistan"] Islamic Republic of Afghanistan
under [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_Afghanistan"] President [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashraf_Ghani"] Ashraf Ghani and reinstating the
 Islamic Emirate of Afghanistan under the control of the
Taliban. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/US%E2%80%93Taliban_deal"] US–Taliban deal, signed on 29 February
2020 in Qatar, was one of the critical events that caused
the collapse of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghan_National_Security_Forces"] Afghan National Security Forces
(ANSF).[32] Following the deal, the US dramatically
reduced the number of air attacks and deprived the
 ANSF of a critical edge in fighting the Taliban
insurgency, leading to the Taliban takeover of
Kabul.[33] Soon after, former [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vice_President_of_Afghanistan"] first vice president
 Amrullah Saleh declared himself the caretaker president
 of Afghanistan and announced the resistance against the
Taliban.[34][35]
Afghanistan is prominently rich in natural resources.
Those resources include lithium, iron, zinc, and copper,
amongst many others. It is also the largest producer of
opium.[36] The country is a founding member of the
 United Nations, the Organisation of Islamic 
 unrecognized
government[3]

Etymology
Some scholars suggest that the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Root_(linguistics)"] root name "[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghan_(ethnonym)"] Afghān" is derived from the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanskrit"] Sanskrit word [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A%C5%9Bvaka"] Aśvakan or Assakan
which was the name used for ancient inhabitants of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindu_Kush"] Hindu Kush.[37] Aśvakan literally means
"horsemen", "horse breeders", or "cavalrymen" (from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A%C5%9Bva"] aśva or aspa, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanskrit"] Sanskrit and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avestan"] Avestan words for
"horse").[38] However, others such as Ibrahim Khan, have contended that the word Afghan comes from
Bactrian. [39]
Historically, the ethnonym Afghān was used to refer to ethnic Pashtuns.[40] The Arabic and Persian form of
the name, Afġān, was first attested in the 10th-century geography book [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hudud_al-%27Alam"] Hudud al-'Alam.[41] The last part of
the name, "[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/-stan"] -stan" is a Persian suffix for "place of". Therefore, "Afghanistan" translates to "land of the
 Afghans", or "land of the Pashtuns" in a historical sense. According to the third edition of the Encyclopedia
of Islam:[42]
The name Afghanistan (Afghānistān, land of the Afghans/Pashtuns, afāghina, sing. afghān)
can be traced to the early eighth/fourteenth century, when it designated the easternmost part of
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kartid"] Kartid realm. This name was later used for certain regions in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Safavid_Iran"] Ṣafavid and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mughal_Empire"] Mughal
empires that were inhabited by Afghans. While based on a state-supporting elite of
 Abdālī/Durrānī Afghans, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Durrani_Empire"] Sadūzāʾī Durrānī polity that came into being in 1160/1747 was
not called Afghanistan in its own day. The name became a state designation only during the
colonial intervention of the nineteenth century.
History
Page 5
Many empires and kingdoms have also risen to power in
Afghanistan, such as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greco-Bactrians"] Greco-Bactrians, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Scythians"] Indo-Scythians,
 Kushans, Kidarites, Hephthalites, Alkhons, Nezaks, Zunbils, Turk
Shahis, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindu_Shahi"] Hindu Shahis, Lawiks, Saffarids, Samanids, Ghaznavids,
Ghurids, Khaljis, Kartids, Lodis, Surs, Mughals, and finally, the
 Hotak and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Durrani_Empire"] Durrani dynasties, which marked the political origins of
the modern state.[43] Throughout millennia several cities within the
modern day Afghanistan served as capitals of various empires,
namely, Bactra (Balkh), Alexandria on the Oxus ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ai-Khanoum"] Ai-Khanoum),
Kapisi, Sigal, Kabul, Kunduz, Zaranj, Firozkoh, Herat, Ghazna
(Ghazni), Binban (Bamyan), and Kandahar. 
Tents of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghans"] Afghan [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nomad"] nomads in the
northern [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Badghis_Province"] Badghis province of
Afghanistan. Early peasant farming
The country has been home to various peoples through the ages,
among them the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Iranian_peoples"] ancient Iranian peoples who established the 
villages came into existence in
Afghanistan about 7,000 years ago.
dominant role of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Iranian_languages"] Indo-Iranian languages in the region. At multiple
points, the land has been incorporated within vast regional empires; among them the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire"] Achaemenid Empire,
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macedonian_Empire"] Macedonian Empire, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maurya_Empire"] Maurya Empire, and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Empire"] Islamic Empire.[44] For its success in resisting foreign
occupation during the 19th and 20th centuries, Afghanistan has been called the "[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graveyard_of_empires_(Afghanistan)"] graveyard of empires",[45]
though it is unknown who coined the phrase.[46]
Prehistory and antiquity
Excavations of prehistoric sites suggest that humans were living in what is now Afghanistan at least 50,000
years ago, and that farming communities in the area were among the earliest in the world. An important site
of early historical activities, many believe that Afghanistan compares to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt"] Egypt in terms of the historical
value of its archaeological sites.[47][48]
Ancient era
 Archaeological exploration done in the 20th century suggests
that the geographical area of Afghanistan has been closely
connected by culture and trade with its neighbors to the east,
west, and north. Artifacts typical of the Paleolithic,
Mesolithic, Neolithic, Bronze, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iron_Age"] Iron Ages have been
found in Afghanistan. Urban civilization is believed to have
begun as early as 3000 BCE, and the early city of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mundigak"] Mundigak
(near [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kandahar"] Kandahar in the south of the country) was a center of
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Helmand_culture"] Helmand culture. More recent findings established that
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indus_Valley_Civilization"] Indus Valley Civilization stretched up towards modern- The extent of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indus_Valley_Civilization"] Indus Valley Civilization
day Afghanistan, making the ancient civilization today part during its mature phase
of Pakistan, Afghanistan, and India. In more detail, it
extended from what today is northwest Pakistan to northwest
India and northeast Afghanistan. An Indus Valley site has been found on the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxus_River"] Oxus River at [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shortugai"] Shortugai in
northern Afghanistan.[49][50] There are several smaller IVC colonies to be found in Afghanistan as well.
An Indus Valley site has been found on the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxus_River"] Oxus River at [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shortugai"] Shortugai in northern Afghanistan, shows
Afghanistan to have been a part of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indus_Valley_Civilization"] Indus Valley Civilization.[51]
After 2000 BCE, successive waves of semi-nomadic people from Central Asia began moving south into
Afghanistan; among them were many [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-European_languages"] Indo-European-speaking [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Iranians"] Indo-Iranians. These tribes later migrated
further into South Asia, Western Asia, and toward Europe via the area north of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caspian_Sea"] Caspian Sea. The region
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kunduz"]
Page 6
at the time was referred to as Ariana.[47][52]
By the middle of the 6th century BCE, the Achaemenids overthrew
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medes"] Medes and incorporated Arachosia, Aria, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bactria"] Bactria within its
 eastern boundaries. An inscription on the tombstone of Darius I of
Persia mentions the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kabulistan"] Kabul Valley in a list of the 29 countries that he
had conquered.[53] The region of Arachosia, around [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kandahar"] Kandahar in
modern-day southern Afghanistan, used to be primarily Zoroastrian
and played a key role in the transfer of the Avesta to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persis"] Persia and is
thus considered by some to be the "second homeland of
Zoroastrianism".[54][55][56]
A "Bactrian gold" [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scythian"] Scythian belt  [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_the_Great"] Alexander the Great and his Macedonian forces arrived in
depicting Dionysus, from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tillya_Tepe"] Tillya Tepe Afghanistan in 330 BCE after defeating [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Darius_III_of_Persia"] Darius III of Persia a year
in the ancient region of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bactria"] Bactria earlier in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Gaugamela"] Battle of Gaugamela. Following Alexander's brief
occupation, the successor state of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seleucid_Empire"] Seleucid Empire controlled
 the region until 305 BCE when they gave much of it to the Maurya
Empire as part of an alliance treaty. The Mauryans controlled the area south of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindu_Kush"] Hindu Kush until they
were overthrown in about 185 BCE. Their decline began 60 years after [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashoka"] Ashoka's rule ended, leading to the
 Hellenistic reconquest by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greco-Bactrians"] Greco-Bactrians. Much of it soon broke away from them and became part of
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Greek_Kingdom"] Indo-Greek Kingdom. They were defeated and expelled by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Scythians"] Indo-Scythians in the late 2nd century
BCE.[57][58]
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silk_Road"] Silk Road appeared during the first century BCE, and
Afghanistan flourished with trade, with routes to China, India,
Persia and north to the cities of Bukhara, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samarkand"] Samarkand and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khiva"] Khiva in
present-day Uzbekistan.[59] Goods and ideas were exchanged at
this center point, such as Chinese silk, Persian silver and Roman
gold, while the region of present Afghanistan was mining and
trading [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lapis_lazuli"] lapis lazuli stones[60] mainly from the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Badakhshan"] Badakhshan region.
During the first century BCE, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parthian_Empire"] Parthian Empire subjugated the
region but lost it to their [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Parthian"] Indo-Parthian vassals. In the mid-to-late
first century CE the vast [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kushan_Empire"] Kushan Empire, centered in Afghanistan,
became great patrons of Buddhist culture, making [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddhism"] Buddhism
flourish throughout the region. The Kushans were overthrown by
 the Sassanids in the 3rd century CE, though the Indo-
Sassanids continued to rule at least parts of the region.
They were followed by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kidarite"] Kidarites who, in turn, was
replaced by the Hephthalites. They were replaced by
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turk_Shahi"] Turk Shahi in the 7th century. The Buddhist Turk
Shahi of Kabul was replaced by a Hindu dynasty 
 BYZANTINE
EMPIRE
before the Saffarids conquered the area in 870, this
Hindu dynasty was called [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindu_Shahi"] Hindu Shahi.[61] Much of
the northeastern and southern areas of the country
remained dominated by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddhist"] Buddhist culture.[62][63]
