Medieval history  The Imperial [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hephthalites"] Hephthalites c. 500 CE
Islamic conquest
Page 7
 Arab [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim"] Muslims brought Islam to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herat"] Herat and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zaranj"] Zaranj in 642 CE and
began spreading eastward; some of the native inhabitants they
 encountered accepted it while others revolted. Before the arrival of
Islam, the region used to be home to various beliefs and cults, often
resulting in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syncretism"] Syncretism between the dominant religions[64][65] such
as Zoroastrianism,[54][55][56] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddhism"] Buddhism or [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greco-Buddhism"] Greco-Buddhism,
 Ancient Iranian religions,[66] Hinduism, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianity"] Christianity[67][68] and
Judaism.[69][70] An exemplification of the syncretism in the region
 Saffarid rule at its greatest extent
under [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ya%27qub_ibn_al-Layth_al-Saffar"] Ya'qub ibn al-Layth al-Saffar 
would be that people were patrons of Buddhism but still
worshipped local Iranian gods such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahura_Mazda"] Ahura Mazda, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nana_(Kushan_goddess)"] Lady Nana,
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anahita"] Anahita or [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mithra"] Mihr(Mithra) and portrayed [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_mythology"] Greek Gods like [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heracles"] Heracles
or [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tyche"] Tyche as protectors of Buddha.[71][66][72] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zunbils"] Zunbils and
Kabul Shahi were first conquered in 870 CE by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saffarid_dynasty"] Saffarid Muslims of Zaranj. Later, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samanids"] Samanids
extended their Islamic influence south of the Hindu Kush. It is reported that Muslims and non-Muslims still
lived side by side in Kabul before the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghaznavids"] Ghaznavids rose to power in the 10th century.[73][74][75]
By the 11th century, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahmud_of_Ghazni"] Mahmud of Ghazni defeated the remaining Hindu rulers and effectively [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamized"] Islamized the
wider region,[76] with the exception of Kafiristan.[77] Mahmud made [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghazni"] Ghazni into an important city and
patronized intellectuals such as the historian [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Biruni"] Al-Biruni and the poet Ferdowsi.[78] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghaznavid_dynasty"] Ghaznavid dynasty
was overthrown by the Ghurids, whose architectural achievements included the remote [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minaret_of_Jam"] Minaret of Jam.
 The Ghurids controlled Afghanistan for less than a century before being conquered by the Khwarazmian
dynasty in 1215.[79]
Mongols and Babur with the Lodi Dynasty
 In 1219 CE, Genghis Khan and his Mongol army overran
the region. His troops are said to have annihilated the
Khwarazmian cities of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herat"] Herat and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balkh"] Balkh as well as
Bamyan.[80] The destruction caused by the Mongols forced
many locals to return to an agrarian rural society.[81] Mongol
rule continued with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ilkhanate"] Ilkhanate in the northwest while the
 Khalji dynasty administered the Afghan tribal areas south of
the Hindu Kush until the invasion of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timur"] Timur (aka Tamerlane),
who established the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timurid_Empire"] Timurid Empire in 1370. Under the rule
of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shah_Rukh"] Shah Rukh the city served as the focal point of the
 Timurid Renaissance, whose glory matched [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Florence"] Florence of the
 Italian Renaissance as the center of a cultural rebirth.[82][83] 
 Mongol invasions and conquests
depopulated large areas of Afghanistan
In the early 16th century, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Babur"] Babur arrived from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferghana"] Ferghana and captured Kabul from the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arghun_dynasty"] Arghun dynasty.[84]
 Babur would go on to conquer the Afghan Lodi dynasty who had ruled the Delhi Sultanate in the First
Battle of Panipat.[85] Between the 16th and 18th century, the Uzbek [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khanate_of_Bukhara"] Khanate of Bukhara, Iranian Safavids,
and Indian [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mughals"] Mughals ruled parts of the territory.[86] During the Medieval Period, the northwestern area of
Afghanistan was referred to by the regional name Khorasan. Two of the four capitals of Khorasan ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herat"] Herat
and Balkh) are now located in Afghanistan, while the regions of Kandahar, Zabulistan, Ghazni,
Kabulistan, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Name_of_Afghanistan"] Afghanistan formed the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frontier"] frontier between Khorasan and Hindustan. However, up to the
 19th century the term Khorasan was commonly used among natives to describe their country; Sir George
Elphinstone wrote with amazement that the country known to outsiders as "Afghanistan" was referred to
by its own inhabitants as "Khorasan" and that the first Afghan official whom he met at the border
welcomed him to Khorasan.[87][88][89][90]
Page 8
Modern history
Hotak Dynasty
In 1709, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mirwais_Hotak"] Mirwais Hotak, a local [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghilzai"] Ghilzai tribal leader,
successfully rebelled against the Safavids. He defeated
 Gurgin Khan and established his own kingdom.[91]
Mirwais died of natural causes in 1715 and was
succeeded by his brother [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdul_Aziz_Hotak"] Abdul Aziz, who was soon
killed by Mirwais' son [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahmud_Hotak"] Mahmud for possibly planning
to concede territories back to the Safavids. Mahmud
led the Afghan army in 1722 to the Persian capital of
Isfahan, captured the city after the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Gulnabad"] Battle of Gulnabad
and proclaimed himself King of Persia.[91] The
 Afghan dynasty was ousted from Persia by Nader
Shah after the 1729 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Damghan_(1729)"] Battle of Damghan. 
Map of the Hotak Empire during the Reign of
 Mirwais Hotak, 1715.
Fall of the Hotak Dynasty
In 1738, Nader Shah and his [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afsharid_dynasty"] forces captured
Kandahar in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Kandahar"] Siege of Kandahar, the last Hotak
stronghold, from Shah [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussain_Hotak"] Hussain Hotak. Soon after, the
Persian and Afghan forces [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nader_Shah%27s_invasion_of_India"] invaded India, Nader Shah
had plundered Delhi, alongside his 16 year old
commander, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmad_Shah_Durrani"] Ahmad Shah Durrani who had assisted
him on these campaigns. Nader Shah was assassinated
in 1747.[92][93]
Rise of the Durrani Empire
 After the death of Nader Shah in 1747, Ahmad Shah Map of the Hotak Empire at its height in 1728.
Durrani had returned to Kandahar with a contingent of  Disputed between [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussain_Hotak"] Hussain Hotak (Centered in
4,000 Pashtuns. The Abdalis had "unanimously Kandahar) and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashraf_Hotak"] Ashraf Hotak (centered in Isfahan)
accepted" Ahmad Shah as their new leader. With his
acension in 1747, Ahmad Shah had led multiple
campaigns against the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mughal_Empire"] Mughal Empire, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maratha_Empire"] Maratha Empire, and then receding, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afsharid_Empire"] Afsharid Empire. Ahmad Shah
had captured [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kabul"] Kabul and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peshawar"] Peshawar from the Mughal appointed governor, Nasir Khan. Ahmad Shah had
then conquered [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herat"] Herat in 1750, and had also captured [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kashmir"] Kashmir in 1752.[94] Ahmad Shah had launched two
campaigns into Khorasan, (1750–1751) and (1754–1755).[95] His first campaign had seen the siege of
Mashhad, however he was forced to retreat after 4 months. In November 1750, he moved to siege
Nishapur, however he was unable to capture the city and was forced to retreat in early 1751. Ahmad Shah
returned in 1754, he captured Tun, and on 23 July, he sieged [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mashhad"] Mashhad once again. Mashhad had fallen on
2 December, however Shah rokh was reappointed in 1755. He was forced to give up Torshiz, Bakharz,
Jam, Khaf, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Torbat-e_Heydarieh"] Turbat-e Haidari to the Afghans. Following this, Ahmad Shah had sieged [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khanate_of_Nishapur"] Nishapur once
again, and captured it.
Objectives and Invasions of India
Page 9
Ahmad Shah invaded India 8 times during his reign. With the
capture of Peshawar, Ahmad Shah had used this as a convenient
striking point to lead his military campaigns into [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Punjab"] Punjab and India.
Ahmad Shah had sought out multiple reasons for his invasions,
Ahmad Shah saw Afghanistan in a dire state, and one that needed
to expand and exploit a weak but rich neighboring country, which
Ahmad Shah had capitalized on in multiple opportunities during his
Invasions of India, he sought the reasons needed to fill his treasury
in a war-plunder conquest based economy.[96] Ahmad Shah had
launched his first invasion in 1748, crossing the indus river, his
armies sacked and absorbed [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lahore"] Lahore into the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Durrani_Empire"] Durrani Realm.
 Ahmad Shah had met Mughal armies at the Battle of Manupur
(1748), where he was defeated and forced to retreat to back to
Afghanistan.[97] Ahmad Shah had returned the next year in 1749,
where he had captured the area around [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lahore"] Lahore and Punjab,
presenting it as an Afghan victory for this campaign. From 1749 to
1767, Ahmad Shah would lead 6 more invasions, the most
important being his sixth invasion, with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Third_Battle_of_Panipat"] Third Battle of Panipat,
which created a power vacumn in northern India, halting [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maratha_Empire"] Maratha
expansion. 
Portrait of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmad_Shah_Durrani"] Ahmad Shah Durrani
c. 1757.
Death of Ahmad Shah and his Successors
Ahmad Shah Durrani had died in October 1772, what followed would be a civil war in succession, with
his named successor, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timur_Shah_Durrani"] Timur Shah Durrani succeeding him after the defeat of his brother, Suleiman
Mirza.[98]
 Timur Shah Durrani ascended to the throne in November 1772, having defeated a coalition under Shah
Wali Khan, the influential prime minister of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Durrani_Empire"] Durrani Empire, and Humayun Mirza. Timur Shah began
his reign by consolidating power toward himself and people loyal to him, purging Durrani Sardars and
influential tribal leaders in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kabul"] Kabul and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kandahar"] Kandahar to bring support toward himself. Timur Shah's reforms also
saw the capital of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Durrani_Empire"] Durrani Empire being shifted from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kandahar"] Kandahar to Kabul, being able to cover the
empire better as a base of ordination since it was essentially the heartland of the empire. This reform saw
 Kabul as the modern capital of Afghanistan today. Having consolidated power to himself, Timur Shah
would fight multiple series of rebellions to consolidate and hold the empire apart, Timur Shah would also
lead campaigns into [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Punjab"] Punjab against the Sikhs like his father did, however being more successful. Most
prominent example of his battles during this campaign would be where Timur Shah led his forces under
Zangi Khan Durrani, with over 18,000 men total of Afghan, Qizilbash, and Mongol cavalrymen. Against
over 60,000 Sikh men. The Sikhs would lose over 30,000 in this battle and would stage a Durrani
resurgence in Punjab.[99] The Durranis lost [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multan"] Multan in 1772 after Ahmad Shah's death, following this
victory by Timur Shah, Timur Shah was able to lay siege to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multan"] Multan and recapture it,[100] incorporating it
into the Durrani empire once again, reintegrating it as a province until the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Multan_(1818)"] Siege of Multan (1818). Timur
Shah would be succeeded by his son, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zaman_Shah_Durrani"] Zaman Shah Durrani after his death on 18 or 20 May 1793. Timur
Shah's reign oversaw the attempted stabilization and consolidation of the empire. However, Timur Shah
had over 24 sons, a mistake that would plunge the empire in civil war over succession crises.[101]
 Zaman Shah Durrani would succeed to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Durrani_Empire"] Durrani Throne following the death of his father, Timur Shah
Durrani. This instigated civil war with his brothers, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahmud_Shah_Durrani"] Mahmud Shah Durrani, and Humayun Mirza revolting
against him. With Humayun centered in Kandahar, and Mahmud Shah centered in Herat.[102] Zaman Shah
would defeat Humayun and also force the loyalty of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahmud_Shah_Durrani"] Mahmud Shah Durrani.[102] Securing his position on
Page 10
the throne, Zaman Shah had led 3 campaigns into Punjab, with the first two campaigns capturing Lahore,
but being forced to retreat due to issues from a possible [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qajar_Iran"] Qajar invasion, or his brother, Mahmud Shah
Durrani revolting. Zaman Shah embarked on his third campaign for [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Punjab"] Punjab in 1800 to deal with a
rebellious Ranjit Singh.[103] However, he was forced to withdraw, with his brother, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahmud_Shah_Durrani"] Mahmud Shah Durrani
 revolting, Zaman Shah would be toppled from his reign, replaced by his brother, Mahmud Shah
Durrani.[103] However, just under 2 years in his reign, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahmud_Shah_Durrani"] Mahmud Shah Durrani would be deposed by his
 brother, Shah Shuja Durrani, on 13 July 1803.[104] Shah Shuja would attempt to consolidate the Durrani
Realm, which had been long striven by civil war. Shah Shuja would later be deposed by his brother at the
 Battle of Nimla (1809),[105] where [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahmud_Shah_Durrani"] Mahmud Shah Durrani would defeat and force Shah Shuja to flee, with
Shah Mahmud usurping the throne again for his second reign beginning on 3 May 1809.[106]
Barakzai dynasty and British wars
Afghan tribesmen in 1841, painted by
British officer [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Rattray"] James Rattray 
By the early 19th century, the Afghan empire was under threat
from the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qajar_dynasty"] Persians in the west and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sikh_Empire"] Sikh Empire in the east.
Afghanistan was divided, including the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herat_(1793-1863)"] Emirate of Herat centered
in the east. Fateh Khan, leader of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barakzai_dynasty"] Barakzai tribe, installed many
of his brothers in positions of power throughout the empire, mostly
ruling as governors of major cities and provinces. After his murder
for apparent treason against the Durrani king. Fateh Khan would be
sentenced by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahmud_Shah_Durrani"] Mahmud Shah Durrani, having him executed. His
brothers rebelled and divided up the provinces of the empire
between themselves. During this turbulent period, Afghanistan had
many temporary rulers until [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dost_Mohammad_Khan"] Dost Mohammad Khan declared
himself emir in 1826.[107] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Punjab"] Punjab and
 Kashmir were lost to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ranjit_Singh"] Ranjit Singh,
who invaded [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khyber_Pakhtunkhwa"] Khyber Pakhtunkhwa in
March 1823 and captured the city of
 Peshawar at  the Battle of
Nowshera.[108] In 1837, during the
 Battle of Jamrud near the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khyber_Pass"] Khyber Pass,
 Akbar Khan and the Afghan army
failed to capture the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jamrud_Fort"] Jamrud Fort from
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sikh_Khalsa_Army"] Sikh Khalsa Army, but killed Sikh
Commander [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hari_Singh_Nalwa"] Hari Singh Nalwa, thus
ending the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghan-Sikh_Wars"] Afghan-Sikh Wars. By this
time the British were advancing from
the east and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Anglo-Afghan_War"] first major conflict
during "[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Great_Game"] the Great Game" was
initiated.[109]
In 1838, a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Army"] British expeditionary force
marched into Afghanistan and arrested
 Dost Mohammad, sent him into exile
 in India and replaced him with Shah
Shuja, the former [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_heads_of_state_of_Afghanistan"] Durrani king as a
puppet on the throne.[110][111]
Following an uprising that saw the
 assassination of Shah Shuja, the 1842
retreat from Kabul of British-Indian 
Map of Afghanistan (Emirate) and surrounding nations in 1860,
 following the conquest of Kandahar, and before the conquest of
Herat.
Page 11
forces and the annihilation of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_George_Keith_Elphinstone"] Elphinstone's army, and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Kabul_(1842)"] Battle of Kabul that led to its recapture, the
British gave up on their attempts to try and subjugate Afghanistan, and allowed Dost Mohammad Khan as
ruler and withdrew their military forces from Afghanistan. Dost Mohammad Khan would spend most of his
reign consolidating the parts of Afghanistan that were lost in the Durrani civil wars. Dost Mohammad Khan
would launch numerous campaigns, and also be able to reunite the Afghan realm in his reign, securing
 Herat in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herat_Campaign_of_1862%E2%80%9363"] Herat Campaign of 1862–63. Dost Mohammad died on 9 June 1863, a few months after his
 campaign to capture Herat. Dost Mohammad's successors would fight for the throne of Afghanistan,
 between Sher Ali Khan, Mohammad Afzal Khan, and Mohammad Azam Khan in the Afghan Civil War
(1863–1869). Sher Ali would win this civil war and would go on to rule the realm until In 1878, the British
had returned in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Anglo-Afghan_War"] Second Anglo-Afghan War which was fought over perceived Russian influence in the
region, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdur_Rahman_Khan"] Abdur Rahman Khan replaced [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammad_Ayub_Khan_(Emir_of_Afghanistan)"] Ayub Khan who had succeeded [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sher_Ali_Khan"] Sher Ali Khan after his death in
1879. Britain would gain control of Afghanistan's foreign relations as part of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Gandamak"] Treaty of Gandamak of
1879, making it an official [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Protectorate"] British Protected State.[112] In 1893, Amir Abdur Rahman signed an agreement
in which the ethnic [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pashtun"] Pashtun and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baloch_people"] Baloch territories were divided by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Durand_Line"] Durand Line, which forms the
modern-day border between Pakistan and Afghanistan. Shia-dominated [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hazarajat"] Hazarajat and pagan [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kafiristan"] Kafiristan
remained politically independent until being [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_conquests_of_Afghanistan"] conquered by Abdur Rahman Khan in 1891–1896. He was
known as the "Iron Amir" for his features and his ruthless methods against tribes.[113] The Iron Amir
viewed railway and telegraph lines coming from the Russian and British as "[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trojan_horse"] trojan horses" and therefore
 prevented railway development in Afghanistan.[114] He died in 1901, succeeded by his son, Habibullah
Khan.
How can a small power like Afghanistan, which is like a goat between these lions [Britain and
Russia] or a grain of wheat between two strong millstones of the grinding mill, [could] stand in
the midway of the stones without being ground to dust?
— Abdur [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdur_Rahman_Khan"] Rahman Khan, the "Iron Amir", in 1900[115][116]
During the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_World_War"] First World War, when Afghanistan was neutral, Habibullah Khan was met by officials of the
Central Powers in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Niedermayer%E2%80%93Hentig_Expedition"] Niedermayer–Hentig Expedition, to declare full independence from the United
Kingdom, join them and attack British India, as part of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindu%E2%80%93German_Conspiracy"] Hindu–German Conspiracy. Their efforts to
bring Afghanistan into the Central Powers failed, but it caused discontent among the population for keeping
neutrality against the British. Habibullah was assassinated during a hunting trip in February 1919, and
 Amanullah Khan eventually assumed power. A staunch supporter of the 1915–1916 expeditions,
Amanullah Khan provoked the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Third_Anglo-Afghan_War"] Third Anglo-Afghan War, entering British India via the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khyber_Pass"] Khyber Pass.[117]
After the end of the Third Anglo-Afghan War and the signing of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anglo-Afghan_Treaty_of_1919"] Treaty of Rawalpindi on 19 August
1919, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emir_of_Afghanistan"] Emir Amanullah Khan declared the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emirate_of_Afghanistan"] Emirate of Afghanistan a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sovereign_state"] sovereign and fully [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Independent_state"] independent state.
He moved to end his country's traditional isolation by establishing diplomatic relations with the
international community, particularly with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union"] Soviet Union and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weimar_Republic"] Weimar Republic of
Germany.[118][119] He proclaimed himself [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King_of_Afghanistan"] King of Afghanistan on 9 June 1926, when the Emirate of
Afghanistan became the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Afghanistan"] Kingdom of Afghanistan. Following a 1927–28 tour of Europe and Turkey, he
introduced several reforms intended to modernize his nation. A key force behind these reforms was
 Mahmud Tarzi, an ardent supporter of the education of women. He fought for Article 68 of Afghanistan's
1923 constitution, which made elementary education compulsory. The institution of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slavery"] slavery was abolished
in the Emirate of Afghanistan in 1923.[120] King Amanullah's wife, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soraya_Tarzi"] Queen Soraya, was an important figure
during this period in the fight for woman's education and against their oppression.[121]
Some of the reforms that were put in place, such as the abolition of the traditional [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Burqa"] burqa for women and the
opening of several co-educational schools, quickly alienated many tribal and religious leaders, and this led
to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghan_Civil_War_(1928%E2%80%931929)"] Afghan Civil War (1928–1929). Faced with the overwhelming armed opposition, King Amanullah
abdicated in January 1929, and soon after Kabul fell to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saqqawist"] Saqqawist forces led by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Habibullah_Kalakani"] Habibullah Kalakani.[122]
Page 12
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emir_of_Afghanistan"] Emir [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amanullah_Khan"] Amanullah invaded
British India in 1919 and
proclaimed Afghanistan's full
independence thereafter. He
 proclaimed himself King of
Afghanistan in June 1926. 
 Prince [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammed_Nadir_Shah"] Mohammed Nadir Shah, Amanullah's cousin, in turn defeated and
killed Kalakani in October 1929, and was declared King Nadir Shah.[123]
He abandoned the reforms of King Amanullah in favor of a more gradual
approach to modernization, but was assassinated in 1933 by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdul_Khaliq_Hazara_(assassin)"] Abdul Khaliq,
a fifteen-year-old [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hazara_people"] Hazara student who was an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amanullah_loyalist"] Amanullah loyalist.[124]
 Mohammed Zahir Shah, Nadir Shah's 19-year-old son, succeeded to the
 throne and reigned as King from 1933 to 1973. The tribal revolts of 1944–
1947 saw King Zahir's reign challenged by Zadran, Safi, Mangal, and
 Wazir tribesmen led by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mazrak_Zadran"] Mazrak Zadran, Salemai, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Faqir_Ipi"] Mirzali Khan, among
others, many of whom were [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amanullah_loyalist"] Amanullah loyalists. Close relations with the
Muslim states Turkey, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hashemite_Kingdom_of_Iraq"] Hashemite Kingdom of Iraq and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pahlavi_dynasty"] Iran/Persia were
also pursued, while further international relations were sought by joining
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/League_of_Nations"] League of Nations in 1934. The 1930s saw the development of roads,
infrastructure, the founding of a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Da_Afghanistan_Bank"] national bank, and increased education.
Road links in the north played a large part in a growing cotton and textile
industry.[125] The country built close relationships with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Axis_powers"] Axis powers,
with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany"] Nazi Germany having the largest share in Afghan development at the
time, along with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy"] Kingdom of Italy and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Empire_of_Japan"] Empire of Japan.[126]
Contemporary history
Until 1946, King Zahir ruled with the assistance of his uncle, who held the
post of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Afghanistan"] Prime Minister and continued the policies of Nadir Shah. Another
of Zahir Shah's uncles, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shah_Mahmud_Khan"] Shah Mahmud Khan, became Prime Minister in
1946 and began an experiment allowing greater political freedom, but
reversed the policy when it went further than he expected. He was replaced
in 1953 by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammed_Daoud_Khan"] Mohammed Daoud Khan, the king's cousin and brother-in-law,
and a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pashtun"] Pashtun nationalist who sought the creation of a Pashtunistan, leading
to highly tense relations with Pakistan.[127] During his ten years at the post
until 1963, Daoud Khan pressed for social modernization reforms and
 sought a closer relationship with the Soviet Union. Afterward, the 1964
constitution was formed, and the first non-royal Prime Minister was sworn
in.[125]
King Zahir Shah, like his father Nadir Shah, had a policy of maintaining
national independence while pursuing gradual modernization, creating
nationalist feeling, and improving relations with the United Kingdom. 
 King Zahir, the last reigning
monarch of Afghanistan,
who reigned from 1933 until
However, Afghanistan remained neutral and was neither a participant in  1973.
 World War II nor aligned with either power bloc in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War"] Cold War thereafter.
However, it was a beneficiary of the latter rivalry as both the Soviet Union
and the United States vied for influence by building Afghanistan's main highways, airports, and other vital
 infrastructure in the post-war period. On a per capita basis, Afghanistan received more Soviet development
aid than any other country. Afghanistan had, therefore, good relations with both Cold War enemies. In
 1973, while the King was in Italy, Daoud Khan launched a bloodless coup and became the first President
of Afghanistan, abolishing the monarchy.
Democratic Republic and Soviet war
Page 13
 In April 1978, the communist People's
Democratic Party of Afghanistan (PDPA)
seized power in a bloody coup d'état against
then-President [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammed_Daoud_Khan"] Mohammed Daoud Khan, in
what is called the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saur_Revolution"] Saur Revolution. The
PDPA declared the establishment of the
 Democratic Republic of Afghanistan, with its
 first leader named as People's Democratic
 Party general secretary Nur Muhammad Soviet troops in Gardez,
Taraki.[128] This would trigger a series of
events that would dramatically turn
Afghanistan from a poor and secluded (albeit
peaceful) country to a hotbed of international
terrorism.[129] The PDPA initiated various 
Afghanistan in 1987 
 Hezb-i Islami Khalis
fighters in the Sultan
 Valley of Kunar
Province, 1987
social, symbolic and land distribution reforms
that provoked strong opposition, while also
brutally oppressing political dissidents. This
caused unrest and quickly expanded into a
state of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(1978%E2%80%93present)"] civil war by 1979, waged by guerrilla
 mujahideen (and smaller [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maoist"] Maoist guerrillas)
against regime forces countrywide. It quickly
turned into a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proxy_war"] proxy war as the Pakistani
government provided these rebels with covert
training centers, the United States [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Cyclone"] supported them through Pakistan's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inter-Services_Intelligence"] Inter-Services Intelligence (ISI),[130]
and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union"] Soviet Union sent thousands of military advisers to support the PDPA regime.[131] Meanwhile,
there was increasingly hostile friction between the competing factions of the PDPA – the dominant [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khalq"] Khalq
and the more moderate Parcham.[132]
In September 1979, PDPA General Secretary Taraki was assassinated in an internal coup orchestrated by
fellow Khalq member, then-prime minister [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hafizullah_Amin"] Hafizullah Amin, who assumed the new general secretary of the
 People's Democratic Party. The situation in the country deteriorated under Amin and thousands of people
went missing.[133] Displeased with Amin's government, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Army"] Soviet Army invaded the country in December
1979, heading for Kabul and killing Amin just three days later.[134] A Soviet-organized regime, led by
Parcham's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Babrak_Karmal"] Babrak Karmal but inclusive of both factions (Parcham and Khalq), filled the vacuum. Soviet
troops in more substantial numbers were deployed to stabilize Afghanistan under Karmal, marking the
beginning of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Afghan_War"] Soviet–Afghan War.[135] The United States and Pakistan,[130] along with smaller actors
like Saudi Arabia and China, continued supporting the rebels, delivering billions of dollars in cash and
weapons including two thousand [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIM-92_Stinger"] FIM-92 Stinger [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surface-to-air_missiles"] surface-to-air missiles.[136][137] Lasting nine years, the
war caused the deaths of between 562,000[138] and 2 million Afghans,[139][140][141][142][143][144][145] and
displaced about 6 million people who subsequently fled Afghanistan, mainly to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghans_in_Pakistan"] Pakistan and Iran.[146]
Heavy air bombardment destroyed many countryside villages, millions of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Landmine"] landmines were planted,[147] and
 some cities such as Herat and Kandahar were also damaged from bombardment. Pakistan's North-West
Frontier Province functioned as an organizational and networking base for the anti-Soviet Afghan
resistance, with the province's influential [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deobandi"] Deobandi ulama playing a major supporting role in promoting the
'jihad'.[148] After the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_withdrawal_from_Afghanistan"] Soviet withdrawal, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghan_Civil_War_(1989-92)"] civil war ensued until the communist regime under People's
Democratic Party leader [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammad_Najibullah"] Mohammad Najibullah collapsed in 1992.[149][150][151]
The Soviet-Afghan War had drastic social effects on Afghanistan. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Militarization"] militarization of society led to
heavily armed police, private bodyguards, openly armed civil defense groups and other such things
becoming the norm in Afghanistan for decades thereafter.[152] The traditional power structure had shifted
from clergy, community elders, intelligentsia and military in favor of powerful warlords.[153]
Page 14
Post–Cold War conflict
Another civil war broke out after the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peshawar_Accords"] creation of a
dysfunctional coalition [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Afghanistan"] government between
leaders of various mujahideen factions. Amid a
state of  [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anarchy"] anarchy and factional
infighting,[154][155][156] various mujahideen
factions committed widespread rape, murder and
extortion,[155][157][158] while Kabul was heavily
bombarded and partially destroyed by the
fighting.[158] Several failed reconciliations and
alliances occurred between different leaders.[159]
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taliban"] Taliban emerged in September 1994 as a
movement and militia of students (talib) from
Islamic [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Madrassas_in_Pakistan"] madrassas (schools) in Pakistan,[158][160]
who soon had military support from Pakistan.[161]
Taking control of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kandahar"] Kandahar city that year,[158] Development of the civil war from 1992 to late 2001
they conquered more territories until finally
driving out the government of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Burhanuddin_Rabbani"] Rabbani from Kabul in 1996,[162][163] where they established an
 emirate[164] that gained international recognition from 3 countries: Pakistan, Saudi Arabia, and the United
Arab Emirates.[165] The Taliban were condemned internationally for the harsh enforcement of their
interpretation of Islamic [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sharia"] sharia law, which resulted in the brutal treatment of many Afghans, especially
women.[166][167] During their rule, the Taliban and their allies committed massacres against Afghan
civilians, denied UN food supplies to starving civilians and conducted a policy of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scorched_earth"] scorched earth, burning
vast areas of fertile land and destroying tens of thousands of homes.[168][169][170][171][172][173]
 After the fall of Kabul to the Taliban, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmad_Shah_Massoud"] Ahmad Shah Massoud and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdul_Rashid_Dostum"] Abdul Rashid Dostum formed the
 Northern Alliance, later joined by others, to resist the Taliban. Dostum's forces were defeated by the
 Taliban during the Battles of Mazar-i-Sharif in 1997 and 1998; Pakistan's Chief of Army Staff, Pervez
Musharraf, began sending thousands of Pakistanis to help the Taliban defeat the Northern
Alliance.[174][161][175][176][177] By 2000 the Northern Alliance only controlled 10% of territory, cornered
in the north-east. On 9 September 2001, Massoud was assassinated by two Arab [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suicide_attack"] suicide attackers in
 Panjshir Valley. Around 400,000 Afghans died in internal conflicts between 1990 and 2001.[178]
21st century
In October 2001, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_invasion_of_Afghanistan"] United States invaded Afghanistan to remove the Taliban from power after they
refused to hand over [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osama_Bin_Laden"] Osama Bin Laden, the prime suspect of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/September_11_attacks"] September 11 attacks, who was a "guest"
of the Taliban and was operating his [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Qaeda"] al-Qaeda network in Afghanistan.[179][180][181] The majority of
Afghans supported the American invasion of their country.[182][183] During the initial invasion, US and
UK forces bombed al-Qaeda training camps, and later working with the Northern Alliance, the Taliban
regime came to an end.[184]
In December 2001, after the Taliban government was overthrown, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghan_Interim_Administration"] Afghan Interim Administration
under [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamid_Karzai"] Hamid Karzai was formed. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Security_Assistance_Force"] International Security Assistance Force (ISAF) was established by
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UN_Security_Council"] UN Security Council to help assist the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karzai_administration"] Karzai administration and provide basic security.[185][186] By
this time, after two decades of war as well as an acute [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Famine"] famine at the time, Afghanistan had one of the
highest [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infant_mortality"] infant and child mortality rates in the world, the lowest life expectancy, much of the population
were hungry,[187][188][189] and infrastructure was in ruins.[190] Many foreign donors started providing aid
and assistance to rebuild the war-torn country.[191][192]
Page 15
Taliban forces meanwhile began regrouping inside Pakistan, while
 more coalition troops entered Afghanistan to help the rebuilding
process.[193][194] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taliban_insurgency"] Taliban began an insurgency to regain
 control of Afghanistan. Over the next decade, ISAF and Afghan
troops led many offensives against the Taliban, but failed to fully
defeat them. Afghanistan remained one of the poorest countries in
 the world because of a lack of foreign investment, government
corruption, and the Taliban insurgency.[195][196] Meanwhile,
Karzai attempted to unite the peoples of the country,[197] and the
 Afghan government was able to build some democratic structures,
 adopting a constitution in 2004 with the name Islamic Republic of 
U.S. troops and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boeing_CH-47_Chinook"] Chinooks in
Afghanistan, 2008
Afghanistan. Attempts were made, often with the support of
foreign donor countries, to improve the country's economy, healthcare, education, transport, and
agriculture. ISAF forces also began to train the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghan_National_Security_Forces"] Afghan National Security Forces. Following 2002, nearly
five million [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghan_diaspora"] Afghans were repatriated.[198] The number of NATO troops present in Afghanistan peaked at
140,000 in 2011,[199] dropping to about 16,000 in 2018.[200]
In September 2014 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashraf_Ghani"] Ashraf Ghani became president after the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghan_presidential_election,_2014"] 2014 presidential election where for the first
time in Afghanistan's history power was democratically transferred.[201][202][203][204][205] On 28
December 2014, NATO formally ended ISAF combat operations in Afghanistan and transferred full
security responsibility to the Afghan government. The NATO-led [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Resolute_Support"] Operation Resolute Support was formed
the same day as a successor to ISAF.[206][207] Thousands of NATO troops remained in the country to train
and advise Afghan government forces[208] and continue their fight against the Taliban.[209] It was
estimated in 2015 that "about 147,000 people have been killed in the Afghanistan war since 2001. More
than 38,000 of those killed have been civilians".[210] A report titled Body Count concluded that 106,000–
170,000 civilians had been killed as a result of the fighting in Afghanistan at the hands of all parties to the
conflict.[211] 
On 14 April 2021, NATO Secretary General [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jens_Stoltenberg"] Jens Stoltenberg said
 the alliance had agreed to start withdrawing its troops from
Afghanistan by 1 May.[212] Soon after the withdrawal of NATO
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021_Taliban_offensive"] troops started, the Taliban launched an offensive against the
Afghan government, quickly advancing in front of collapsing
Afghan government forces.[213][214] On 15 August 2021, as the
Taliban once again controlled a vast majority of Afghan territory,
they [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fall_of_Kabul_(2021)"] re-captured the capital city of Kabul, and many civilians,
government officials and foreign diplomats were evacuated.[215]
A map of Afghanistan showing the
 2021 Taliban offensive 
President Ghani fled Afghanistan that day.[216] As of 16 August
2021, an unofficial Coordination Council led by senior statesmen
was in the process of coordinating the transfer of the state
institutions of the Islamic Republic of Afghanistan to the
 Taliban.[217] On 17 August, the First Vice President of the Islamic Republic of Afghanistan, Amrullah
 Saleh, proclaimed himself the caretaker President of Afghanistan and announced the formation of an anti-
 Taliban front with a reported 6,000+ troops[218][219] in the Panjshir Valley, along with Ahmad
Massoud.[220][221] However, on 6 September, the Taliban took control of most of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Panjshir_province"] Panjshir province,
with resistance fighters retreating to the mountains to continue fighting within the province.[222] Fights in
the valley ceased mid-September,[223] while resistances leaders [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amrullah_Saleh"] Amrullah Saleh and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmad_Massoud"] Ahmad Massoud fled
to neighboring Tajikistan.[224][225][222]
Page 16
The Islamic Emirate of Afghanistan was swiftly restored as its
opponents were defeated or left the country. It is apparently led by
 supreme leader [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hibatullah_Akhundzada"] Hibatullah Akhundzada[226] and acting [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Afghanistan"] Prime Minister
 Hasan Akhund, who took office on 7 September 2021.[227][228]
Akhund is one of the four founders of the Taliban[229] and was a
deputy Prime Minister in their previous Emirate; his appointment was
 seen as a compromise between moderates and hardliners.[230] A new,
all-male cabinet was formed including [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdul_Hakim_Ishaqzai"] Abdul Hakim Ishaqzai as
 Minister of Justice.[231][232] On 20 September 2021, United Nations
Secretary-General [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres"] António Guterres received a letter from acting
 minister of Foreign Affairs [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amir_Khan_Muttaqi"] Amir Khan Muttaqi to formally claim 
Taliban fighters in Kabul on a
captured [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humvee"] Humvee following the
 2021 fall of Kabul.
Afghanistan's seat as a member state for their official spokesman in
Doha, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suhail_Shaheen"] Suhail Shaheen, and asked to address the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly"] General Assembly. During the previous Taliban rule from
1996 to 2001, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations"] United Nations never recognized their representatives and chose to work with the then-
government in exile instead.[233]
Western nations have suspended most humanitarian aid to Afghanistan following the Taliban's takeover of
the country in August 2021 and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Bank"] World Bank and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund"] International Monetary Fund also halted
 payments.[234][235] In October 2021, more than half of Afghanistan's 39 million people faced an acute food
shortage.[236] On 11 November 2021, the Human Rights Watch reported that Afghanistan was facing
widespread [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Famine"] famine due to an economic and banking crisis.[237]
Geography
Afghanistan is located in Southern-Central Asia.[238][239][240][241][242] The region centered at Afghanistan
is considered the "crossroads of Asia",[243] and the country has had the nickname Heart of Asia.[244] The
renowned [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urdu"] Urdu poet [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allama_Iqbal"] Allama Iqbal once wrote about the country:
Asia is a body of water and earth, of which the Afghan nation is the heart. From its discord,
the discord of Asia; and from its accord, the accord of Asia.
At over 652,864 km2 (252,072 sq mi),[245] Afghanistan is the world's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area"] 41st largest country,[246] slightly
bigger than France and smaller than Myanmar, and about the size of Texas in the United States. There is no
coastline, as Afghanistan is landlocked. Afghanistan shares its longest land border (the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Durand_Line"] Durand Line) with
Pakistan to the east and south, followed by borders with Tajikistan to the north-east, Iran to the west,
Turkmenistan to the north-west, Uzbekistan to the north and China to the north-east; India recognizes a
border with Afghanistan through Pakistani-administered Kashmir.[247] Clockwise from south-west,
Afghanistan shares borders with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sistan_and_Baluchestan_Province"] Sistan and Baluchestan Province, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Khorasan_Province"] South Khorasan Province and
 Razavi Khorasan Province of Iran; [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahal_Region"] Ahal Region, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mary_Region"] Mary Region and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lebap_Region"] Lebap Region of Turkmenistan;
 Surxondaryo Region of Uzbekistan; [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khatlon_Region"] Khatlon Region and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gorno-Badakhshan_Autonomous_Region"] Gorno-Badakhshan Autonomous Region of
 Tajikistan; Xinjiang Uyghur Autonomous Region of China; and the Gilgit-Baltistan territory, Khyber
Pakhtunkhwa province and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balochistan,_Pakistan"] Balochistan province of Pakistan.[248]
The geography in Afghanistan is varied, but is mostly mountainous and rugged, with some unusual
mountain ridges accompanied by plateaus and river basins.[249] It is dominated by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindu_Kush"] Hindu Kush range,
the western extension of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Himalayas"] Himalayas that stretches to eastern [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tibet"] Tibet via the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pamir_Mountains"] Pamir Mountains and
 Karakoram Mountains in Afghanistan's far north-east. Most of the highest points are in the east consisting
of fertile mountain valleys, often considered part of the "[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roof_of_the_World"] Roof of the World". The Hindu Kush ends at the
west-central highlands, creating plains in the north and southwest, namely the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkestan"] Turkestan Plains and the
Page 17
 Sistan Basin; these two regions consist of rolling grasslands and semi-deserts, and hot windy deserts,
 respectively.[250] Forests exist in the corridor between Nuristan and Paktika provinces (see East Afghan
montane conifer forests),[251] and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tundra"] tundra in the north-east. The country's highest point is Noshaq, at
7,492 m (24,580 ft) above sea level.[10] The lowest point lies in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jowzjan_Province"] Jowzjan Province along the Amu River
bank, at 258 m (846 ft) above sea level. 
Despite having numerous rivers and reservoirs,
large parts of the country are dry. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endorheic"] endorheic
Sistan Basin is one of the driest regions in the
world.[252] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amu_Darya"] Amu Darya rises at the north of
the Hindu Kush, while the nearby [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hari_Rud"] Hari Rud flows
west towards Herat, and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arghandab_River"] Arghandab River
from the central region southwards. To the south
and west of the Hindu Kush flow a number of
streams that are tributaries of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indus_River"] Indus River,[249]
such as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Helmand_River"] Helmand River. One exception is the
 Kabul River which flows in an easternly direction
to the Indus ending at the Indian Ocean.[253]
Afghanistan receives heavy snow during the
The mountainous [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Topography"] topography of Afghanistan 
winter in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindu_Kush"] Hindu Kush and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pamir_Mountains"] Pamir Mountains,
and the melting snow in the spring season enters
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_rivers_of_Afghanistan"] rivers, lakes, and streams.[254][255] However,
two-thirds of the country's water flows into the
neighboring countries of Iran, Pakistan, and Turkmenistan. As reported in 2010, the state needs more than
US$2 billion to rehabilitate its irrigation systems so that the water is properly managed.[256]
The northeastern Hindu Kush [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mountain_range"] mountain range, in and around the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Badakhshan_Province"] Badakhshan Province of Afghanistan, is
in a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_environment#Geological_activity"] geologically active area where earthquakes may occur almost every year.[257] They can be deadly and
destructive, causing [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Landslide"] landslides in some parts or [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2009_Afghan_avalanches"] avalanches during the winter.[258] The last strong
earthquakes were in 1998, which killed about 6,000 people in Badakhshan near Tajikistan.[259] This was
followed by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2002_Hindu_Kush_earthquakes"] 2002 Hindu Kush earthquakes in which over 150 people were killed and over 1,000
injured. A [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010_Afghanistan_earthquake"] 2010 earthquake left 11 Afghans dead, over 70 injured, and more than 2,000 houses destroyed.
Climate
Afghanistan has a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continental_climate"] continental climate with harsh winters
in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hazarajat"] central highlands, the glaciated northeast (around
Nuristan), and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wakhan_Corridor"] Wakhan Corridor, where the average
temperature in January is below −15 °C (5 °F) and can
reach −26 °C (−15 °F),[249] and hot summers in the
low-lying areas of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sistan_Basin"] Sistan Basin of the southwest, the
 Jalalabad basin in the east, and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghan_Turkestan"] Turkestan plains
along the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amu_River"] Amu River in the north, where temperatures
average over 35 °C (95 °F) in July[10][261] and can go
over 43 °C (109 °F).[249] The country is generally [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arid"] arid 
 Köppen climate map of Afghanistan[260]
in the summers, with most rainfall falling between December and April. The lower areas of northern and
western Afghanistan are the driest, with precipitation more common in the east. Although proximate to
India, Afghanistan is mostly outside the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monsoon"] monsoon zone,[249] except the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuristan_Province"] Nuristan Province which
occasionally receives summer monsoon rain.[262]
Page 18
Biodiversity
 Several types of mammals exist throughout Afghanistan. Snow
leopards, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siberian_tiger"] Siberian tigers and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brown_bear"] brown bears live in the high elevation
 alpine tundra regions. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marco_Polo_sheep"] Marco Polo sheep exclusively live in the
 Wakhan Corridor region of north-east Afghanistan. Foxes, wolves,
otters, deer, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wild_sheep"] wild sheep, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lynx"] lynx and other big cats populate the
mountain forest region of the east. In the semi-desert northern
plains, wildlife include a variety of birds, hedgehogs, gophers, and
large carnivores such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_jackal"] jackals and hyenas.[263]
Gazelles, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wild_boar"] wild pigs and jackals populate the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steppe"] steppe plains of the
south and west, while [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mongoose"] mongoose and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cheetah"] cheetahs exist in the semi-
desert south.[263] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marmot"] Marmots and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ibex"] ibex also live in the high mountains 
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Snow_leopard"] snow leopard was the official
 national animal of the Islamic
Republic of Afghanistan
of Afghanistan, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pheasant"] pheasants exist in some parts of the
country.[264] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghan_hound"] Afghan hound is a native breed of dog known for its fast speed and its long hair; it is
relatively known in the west.[265]
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endemic"] Endemic fauna of Afghanistan includes the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghan_flying_squirrel"] Afghan flying squirrel, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghan_snowfinch"] Afghan snowfinch, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghanodon"] Afghanodon (or the
"[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paghman"] Paghman mountain salamander"),  [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stigmella_kasyi"] Stigmella kasyi,  [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulcaniella_kabulensis"] Vulcaniella kabulensis,  [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghan_leopard_gecko"] Afghan leopard gecko,
 Wheeleria parviflorellus, amongst others. Endemic flora include [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iris_afghanica"] Iris afghanica. Afghanistan has a wide
variety of birds despite its relatively arid climate – an estimated 460 species of which 235 breed within.[265]
The forest region of Afghanistan has vegetation such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pine_tree"] pine trees, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spruce_tree"] spruce trees, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fir_tree"] fir trees and larches,
whereas the steppe grassland regions consist of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Broadleaf_tree"] broadleaf trees, short grass, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perennial_plant"] perennial plants and shrublands.
The colder high elevation regions are composed of hardy grasses and small flowering plants.[263] Several
regions are designated [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_protected_areas_of_Afghanistan"] protected areas; there are three [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_parks"] national parks: [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Band-e_Amir"] Band-e Amir, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wakhan_National_Park"] Wakhan and Nuristan.
Afghanistan had a 2018 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index"] Forest Landscape Integrity Index mean score of 8.85/10, ranking it 15th globally
out of 172 countries.[266]
Demographics
The population of Afghanistan was estimated at
32.9 million as of 2019 by the Afghanistan Statistics and
Information Authority,[268] whereas the UN estimates
over 38.0 million.[269] In 1979 the total population was
reported to be about 15.5 million.[270] About 23.9% of
them are urbanite, 71.4% live in rural areas, and the
remaining 4.7% are nomadic.[271] An additional
3 million or so Afghans are temporarily housed in
neighboring [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghans_in_Pakistan"] Pakistan and Iran, most of whom were born
and raised in those two countries. As of 2013,
Afghanistan was the largest refugee-producing country
in the world, a title held for 32 years. 
A 2005 CIA map showing traditional Afghan tribal
territories. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pashtun_tribes"] Pashtun tribes form the world's largest
tribal society.[267]
The current population growth rate is 2.37%,[10] one of
the highest in the world outside of Africa. This population is expected to reach 82 million by 2050 if
current population trends continue.[272] The population of Afghanistan increased steadily until the 1980s,
when civil war caused millions to flee to other countries such as Pakistan.[273] Millions have since returned
and the war conditions contribute to the country having the highest fertility rate outside Africa.[274]
Afghanistan's healthcare has recovered since the turn of the century, causing falls in infant mortality and
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuristan_National_Park"]
Page 19
increases in life expectancy, although it has the lowest life expectance of any country outside Africa. This
(along with other factors such as returning refugees) caused rapid population growth in the 2000s that has
only recently started to slow down. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gini_coefficient"] Gini coefficient in 2008 was 27.8.[275]
Ethnicity and languages
 Afghans are divided into several [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnolinguistic"] ethnolinguistic groups.
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pashtuns"] Pashtuns are the largest ethnic group, comprising
 39% (2019 sociological research data by The Asia
Foundation),  followed by Tajiks (or Farsiwans),
comprising 37%.[276] of the country's  population.
Generally the other three major ethnic groups are the
Tajiks, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hazaras"] Hazaras and Uzbeks. A further 10 other ethnic
groups are recognized and each are represented in the
 Afghan National Anthem.[277]
 Dari and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pashto"] Pashto are the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Official_language"] official languages of
Afghanistan; [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bilingualism"] bilingualism is very common.[278] Dari,
which is a variety of and mutually intelligible with
 Persian (and very often called 'Farsi' by some Afghans
like in Iran) functions as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lingua_franca"] lingua franca in Kabul as  Ethnolinguistic map of Afghanistan (2001)
well as in much of the northern and northwestern parts
of the country.[279] Native speakers of Dari, of any
ethnicity, are sometimes called Farsiwans.[280] Pashto is the native tongue of the Pashtuns, although many
of them are also fluent in Dari while some non-Pashtuns are fluent in Pashto. Despite the Pashtuns having
been dominant in Afghan politics for centuries, Dari remained the preferred language for government and
bureaucracy.[281] According to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_World_Factbook"] CIA World Factbook, Dari Persian is spoken by 78% ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_language"] L1 + L2) and
functions as the lingua franca, while Pashto is spoken by 50%, Uzbek 10%, English 5%, Turkmen 2%,
Urdu 2%, Pashayi 1%, Nuristani 1%, Arabic 1%, and Balochi 1% (2021 est). Data represent the most
widely spoken languages; shares sum to more than 100% because there is much bilingualism in the country
and because respondents were allowed to select more than one language.There are a number of smaller
regional languages, including Uzbek, Turkmen, Balochi, Pashayi, and Nuristani.[282]
When it comes to foreign languages among the populace, many are able to speak or understand [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindustani_language"] Hindustani
(Urdu-Hindi), partly due to returning Afghan refugees from Pakistan and the popularity of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bollywood"] Bollywood films
respectively.[283] English is also understood by some of the population,[284] and has been gaining
popularity as of the 2000s.[285] Some Afghans retain some ability in Russian, which was taught in public
schools during the 1980s.[283]
Religion
The CIA estimated in 2009 that 99.7% of the Afghan population was Muslim[10] and most are thought to
adhere to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sunni"] Sunni [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hanafi"] Hanafi school.[286] According to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pew_Research_Center"] Pew Research Center, as much as 90% are of the
Sunni denomination, 7% [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia"] Shia and 3% [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-denominational_Muslim"] non-denominational.[287] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CIA"] CIA Factbook variously estimates up
to 89.7% Sunni or up to 15% Shia.[10] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Izady"] Michael Izady estimated 70% of the population to be followers of
Sunni Islam, 25% [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imamiyyah"] Imami Shia Islam, 4.5% [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isma%27ilism"] Ismaili Shia Islam, and 0.5% [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion_in_Afghanistan#Minority_religious_groups"] other religions.[288]
Afghan [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sikhism_in_Afghanistan"] Sikhs and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hinduism_in_Afghanistan"] Hindus are also found in certain major cities (namely Kabul, Jalalabad, Ghazni,
Kandahar)[289][290] accompanied by gurdwaras and mandirs.[291] According to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deutsche_Welle"] Deutsche Welle in
September 2021, 250 remain in the country after 67 were evacuated to India.[292]
Page 20
There was a small [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Afghanistan"] Jewish community in Afghanistan, living mainly
in Herat and Kabul. Over the years, this small community was
forced leave due to decades of warfare and religious persecution.
By the end of the twentieth century, the entire community had
emigrated to Israel and the United States, with the exception of one
person, Herat-born [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zablon_Simintov"] Zablon Simintov. He remained for years, being
the caretaker of the only remaining Afghan synagogue.[293] After
the second Taliban takeover, he left Afghanistan for the United
States.[294]
 Afghan Christians, who number 500–8,000, practice their faith
secretly due to intense societal opposition, and there are no public
churches.[295][296] 
 Blue Mosque in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mazar-i-Sharif"] Mazar-i-Sharif is the
largest [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mosque"] mosque in Afghanistan
Urbanization
As estimated by the CIA World Factbook, 26% of the population was urbanized as of 2020. This is one of
the lowest figures in the world; in Asia it is only higher than Cambodia, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nepal"] Nepal and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sri_Lanka"] Sri Lanka. Urbanization
has increased rapidly, particularly in the capital Kabul, due to returning refugees from Pakistan and Iran
after 2001, internally displaced people, and rural migrants.[297] Urbanization in Afghanistan is different
from typical urbanization in that it is centered on just a few cities.[298]
The only city with over a million residents is its capital, Kabul, located in the east of the country. The other
large cities are located generally in the "ring" around the Central Highlands, namely [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kandahar"] Kandahar in the south,
 Herat in the west, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mazar-i-Sharif"] Mazar-i-Sharif and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kunduz"] Kunduz in the north, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jalalabad"] Jalalabad in the east.[271]

Education
 Education in Afghanistan includes K–12 and higher education, which is overseen by the Ministry of
Education and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Higher_Education_(Afghanistan)"] Ministry of Higher Education. There are over 16,000 schools in the country and roughly
9 million students. Of this, about 60% are males and 40% females. However, the new regime has thus far
forbidden girls and female teachers from returning to secondary schools.[300][301] Over 174,000 students
are enrolled in different [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Afghanistan"] universities around the country. About 21% of these are females.[302] Former
Education Minister [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghulam_Farooq_Wardak"] Ghulam Farooq Wardak had stated that construction of 8,000 schools is required for the
remaining children who are deprived of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_learning"] formal learning.[303] As of 2018 the literacy rate of the population
Page 21
age 15 and older is 43.02% (males 55.48% and females
29.81%).[304]
 The top universities in Afghanistan are the American
 University of Afghanistan (AUAF) followed by Kabul
University (KU), both of which are located in Kabul. The
 National Military Academy of Afghanistan, modeled after the
 United States Military Academy at West Point, was a four-year
military development institution dedicated to graduating
 officers for the Afghan Armed Forces. The Afghan Defense UNESCO Institute of Statistics
University was constructed near [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qargha"] Qargha in Kabul. Major Afghanistan Literacy Rate population
universities outside of Kabul include [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kandahar_University"] Kandahar University in  plus15 1980–2018
the south, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herat_University"] Herat University in the northwest, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balkh_University"] Balkh University
and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kunduz_University"] Kunduz University in the north, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nangarhar_University"] Nangarhar University and
 Khost University in the east. Kabul University was founded in 1932 and is a respected institute that played
a significant part in the country's education;[305] from the 1960s the Kabul University was also a hotbed of
radical political ideologies such as Marxism and Islamism, which played major parts in society, politics and
the war that began in 1978.[306]
After the Taliban regained power in 2021, it became unclear to what extent female education would
continue in the country. In March 2022, after they had been closed for some time, it was announced that
girl's schools after 6th grade would be reopened shortly. However, shortly before reopening, the order was
rescinded and schools for older girls remained closed.[307]
Health
According to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_Development_Index"] Human Development Index, Afghanistan is the
 15th least developed country in the world. The average life
expectancy is estimated to be around 60 years.[308][309] The
country's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maternal_mortality"] maternal mortality rate is 396 deaths/100,000 live births
and its [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infant_mortality"] infant mortality rate is 66[309] to 112.8 deaths in every 1,000
live births.[10] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Public_Health_(Afghanistan)"] Ministry of Public Health plans to cut the infant
mortality rate to 400 for every 100,000 live births before 2020. The
country has more than 3,000 midwives, with an additional 300 to
400 being trained each year.[310] 
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daoud_Khan_Military_Hospital"] Daoud Khan Military Hospital in
Kabul is one of the largest [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_Afghanistan"] hospitals
There are over 100 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hospitals_in_Afghanistan"] hospitals in Afghanistan,[311] with the most 
in Afghanistan
 advanced treatments being available in Kabul. The French Medical
Institute for Children and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indira_Gandhi_Children%27s_Hospital"] Indira Gandhi Children's Hospital in Kabul are the leading [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Children%27s_hospital"] children's hospitals in
 the country. Some of the other leading hospitals in Kabul include the Jamhuriat Hospital and Jinnah
Hospital.[312] In spite of all this, many Afghans travel to Pakistan and India for advanced treatment.
It was reported in 2006 that nearly 60% of the Afghan population lives within a two-hour walk of the
nearest health facility.[313] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disability"] Disability rate is also high in Afghanistan due to the decades of war.[314] It was
reported recently that about 80,000 people are missing limbs.[315][316] Non-governmental charities such as
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Save_the_Children"] Save the Children and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahboba%27s_Promise"] Mahboba's Promise assist orphans in association with governmental structures.[317]
 Demographic and Health Surveys is working with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Institute_of_Health_Management_Research"] Indian Institute of Health Management Research and
others to conduct a survey in Afghanistan focusing on [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maternal_death"] maternal death, among other things.[318]
Governance
Page 22
 Following the effective collapse of the Islamic Republic of
Afghanistan during the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021_Taliban_offensive"] 2021 Taliban offensive, the Taliban declared
the country an Islamic Emirate. A new caretaker government was
announced on 7 September.[319] As of 8 September 2021, no other
country had formally recognized the Islamic Emirate of Afghanistan as
the de jure government of Afghanistan.[320]
A traditional instrument of governance in Afghanistan is the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Loya_jirga"] loya jirga
(grand assembly),  a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pashtun"] Pashtun consultative meeting that was mainly
organized for choosing a new [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Head_of_state"] head of state, adopting a new
constitution, or to settle national or regional issue such as war.[321]
Loya jirgas have been held since at least 1747,[322] with the most
recent one occurring in August 2020.[323][324] 
 The Arg (the Presidential palace)
in Kabul
Development of Taliban government
On 17 August 2021, the leader of the Taliban-affiliated
 Hezb-e-Islami Gulbuddin party, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulbuddin_Hekmatyar"] Gulbuddin Hekmatyar, met
 with both Hamid Karzai, the former President of
Afghanistan, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdullah_Abdullah"] Abdullah Abdullah, the former chairman of
the High Council for National Reconciliation and former
 Chief Executive, in Doha, Qatar, with the aim of forming a
 national unity government.[325][326] President [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashraf_Ghani"] Ashraf Ghani,
having fled the country during the Taliban advance to either
 Tajikistan or Uzbekistan, emerged in the United Arab
Emirates and said that he supported such negotiations and
was in talks to return to Afghanistan.[327][328] Many figures
within the Taliban generally agreed that continuation of the
 2004 Constitution of Afghanistan may, if correctly applied,
be workable as the basis for the new religious state as their
objections to the former government were political, and not
religious.[329] 
 Hasan Akhund
Acting [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Afghanistan"] Prime Minister 
 Sirajuddin Haqqani
First [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deputy_Leader_of_the_Islamic_Emirate_of_Afghanistan"] Deputy Leader and
Acting [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interior_Minister_of_Afghanistan"] Interior Minister

30 August, a Taliban official interviewed said that a new
government would likely be announced as early as Friday 3
 September after Jumu'ah. It was added that Hibatullah
Akhundzada would be officially named Emir, with cabinet
ministers being revealed at the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arg_(Kabul)"] Arg in an official ceremony.
Abdul Ghani Baradar would be named [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Head_of_government"] head of government
as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Afghanistan"] Prime Minister, while other important positions would go
to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sirajuddin_Haqqani"] Sirajuddin Haqqani and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mullah_Yaqoob"] Mullah Yaqoob. Beneath the
supreme leader, day-to-day governance will be entrusted to
the cabinet.[330]

According to CNN, the new government is likely to be a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unitary_state"] unitary [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deobandi"] Deobandist [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_republic"] Islamic republic. In a report
by CNN-News18, sources said the new government was going to be governed similarly to Iran with
Haibatullah Akhundzada as supreme leader similar to the role of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_Khamenei"] Saayid Ali Khamenei, and would be
based out of Kandahar. Baradar or Yaqoob would be head of government as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_minister"] Prime Minister. The
government's ministries and agencies will be under a cabinet presided over by the Prime Minister. The
Supreme Leader would preside over an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executive_(government)"] executive body known Supreme Council with anywhere from 11 to

to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chief_justice"] Chief Justice. According to the report, the new
government will take place within the framework of an
amended [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1964_Constitution_of_Afghanistan"] 1964 Constitution of Afghanistan.[331]
However, later interviews disclosed to News18 that
negotiations were not yet completed and that representatives
were still in Kandahar, and that the announcement of the new
government would not take place until 4 September or
later.[332][333][334] Government formation was further
delayed with the announcement postponed to some time
during the week of 6 September, due to concerns about
forming a broad-based government acceptable to the
international community.[335] It was later added however that
the Taliban's Rahbari Shura, the group's leadership council
was divided between the hardline Haqqani Network and 
U.S. representative [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zalmay_Khalilzad"] Zalmay Khalilzad (left)

moderate Abdul Ghani Baradar over appointments needed to
form an "inclusive" government. This culminated in a skirmish which led to Baradar being injured and
treated in Pakistan.[336] It was speculated that the government would be announced on 11 September 2021,
the 20th anniversary of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/9/11_attacks"] 9/11 attacks, with invitations possibly being extended to the governments of
Turkey, China, Iran, Pakistan, and Qatar.[337]
As of early September, the Taliban were planning the Cabinet to be men-only, stating that women would
not be allowed to "work in high-ranking posts" in the government and that women were "ruled out" from
the Cabinet. Journalists and other human rights activists, mostly women, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021_Afghan_protests"] protested in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herat"] Herat and Kabul,
calling for women to be included in the Cabinet.[338] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cabinet_of_Afghanistan#Islamic_Emirate_(2021%E2%80%93present)"] acting Cabinet announced on 7 September was
men-only, and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Women%27s_Affairs_(Afghanistan)"] Ministry of Women's Affairs appeared to have been abolished.[319] On March 23, 2022,
there were reports a cabinet shakeup was underway as another meeting of the Leadership Council was held
in Kandahar for the second time since the Taliban Islamic Movement [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fall_of_Kabul_(2021)"] came to power as a way to get
international recognition. The last meeting of the Leadership Council was held from August 28, 2021, to
August 30, 2021.[339][340]
Administrative divisions
Afghanistan is administratively divided into 34 provinces ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilayat"] wilayat).[341] Each province has a governor and
a capital. The country is further divided into nearly 400 provincial districts, each of which normally covers
a city or several villages. Each district is represented by a district governor.
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_current_governors_of_Afghanistan"] provincial governors are now appointed by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Afghanistan"] Prime Minister of Afghanistan, and the district
governors are selected by the provincial governors.[342] The provincial governors are representatives of the
central government in Kabul and are responsible for all administrative and formal issues within their
provinces. There are also provincial councils that are elected through direct and general elections for four
years.[343] The functions of provincial councils are to take part in provincial development planning and to
participate in the monitoring and appraisal of other provincial governance institutions.
According to article 140 of the constitution and the presidential decree on electoral law, mayors of cities
should be elected through free and direct elections for a four-year term. In practice however, mayors are
appointed by the government.[344]
The following is a list of all the 34 provinces in alphabetical order:
