Afghanistan is divided into [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Provinces_of_Afghanistan"] 34 provinces, which are further
divided into a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Districts_of_Afghanistan"] number of districts
Foreign relations
Afghanistan became a member of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations"] United Nations in 1946.[345] Historically, Afghanistan had strong
relations with Germany, one of the first countries to recognize Afghanistan's independence in 1919; the
Soviet Union, which provided much aid and military training for Afghanistan's forces and includes the
signing of a Treaty of Friendship in 1921 and 1978; and India, with which a friendship treaty was signed in
1950.[346] Relations with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghanistan%E2%80%93Pakistan_relations"] Pakistan have often been tense for various reasons such as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Durand_Line"] Durand Line
border issue and alleged Pakistani involvement in Afghan insurgent groups.
Page 25
The present Islamic Emirate of Afghanistan is currently internationally unrecognized, but has had notable
unofficial ties with China, Pakistan, and Qatar.[347][348] Under the previous Islamic Republic of
 Afghanistan, it enjoyed cordial relations with a number of NATO and allied nations, particularly the United
States, Canada, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghanistan%E2%80%93United_Kingdom_relations"] United Kingdom, Germany, Australia, and Turkey. In 2012, the United States and the
then-republic in Afghanistan signed their [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/US%E2%80%93Afghanistan_Strategic_Partnership_Agreement"] Strategic Partnership Agreement in which Afghanistan became a
 major non-NATO ally.[349]
Military
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_the_Islamic_Emirate_of_Afghanistan"] Armed Forces of the Islamic Emirate of Afghanistan captured a large amount of weapons, hardware,
vehicles, aerocrafts, and equipment from the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghan_Armed_Forces"] Afghan Armed Forces following the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021_Taliban_offensive"] 2021 Taliban offensive
and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fall_of_Kabul_(2021)"] Fall of Kabul. The total value of the captured equipment has been estimated at US$83
billion.[350][351]
Human rights
Homosexuality is [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taboo"] taboo in Afghan society;[352] according to the Penal Code, homosexual intimacy is
 punished by up to a year in prison.[353] With implementing Sharia law offenders can be punished by
death.[354][355] However an ancient tradition involving male homosexual acts between youngsters and
older men (typically wealthy or elite people) called [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bacha_bazi"] bacha bazi persists.
Religious minorities such as Sikhs,[356] Hindus,[357] and Christians have reportedly faced persecution in
the country.[358][359]
Since May 2022, all women in Afghanistan have been required by law to wear full-body coverings when
in public (either a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Burqa"] burqa or an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abaya"] abaya paired with a niqāb, which leaves only the eyes uncovered).[360][361]
In a May interview with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christiane_Amanpour"] Christiane Amanpour, First [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deputy_Leader_of_the_Islamic_Emirate_of_Afghanistan"] Deputy Leader [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sirajuddin_Haqqani"] Sirajuddin Haqqani claimed the decree
is only advisory and no form of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hijab"] hijab is compulsory in Afghanistan,[362] though this contradicts the
reality.[363] It has been speculated that there is a genuine internal policy division over women's rights
between hardliners, including Leader Hibatullah Akhundzada, and pragmatists, though they publicly
present a united front.[364] Another decree was issued shortly after the first, requiring female TV presenters
to cover their faces during broadcasts.[365]
In May 2022, the Taliban dissolved Afghanistan's Human Rights Commission along with four other
government departments, citing the country's budget deficit.[366]
Economy
Afghanistan's nominal GDP was $21.7 billion in 2018, or $72.9 billion by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity"] purchasing power parity
(PPP).[20] Its [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita"] GDP per capita is $2,024 (PPP).[20] Despite having $1 trillion or more in mineral
deposits,[367] it remains one of the world's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Least_developed_countries"] least developed countries. Afghanistan's rough physical
geography and its landlocked status has been cited as reasons why the country has always been among the
least developed in the modern era – a factor where progress is also slowed by contemporary conflict and
political instability.[249] The country imports over $7 billion worth of goods but exports only $784 million,
mainly fruits and nuts. It has $2.8 billion in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/External_debt"] external debt.[10] The service sector contributed the most to the
GDP (55.9%) followed by agriculture (23%) and industry (21.1%).[368]
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Niq%C4%81b"]

While the nation's current account deficit is largely financed with
donor money, only a small portion is provided directly to the
government budget. The rest is provided to non-budgetary
expenditure and donor-designated projects through the United
Nations system and non-governmental organizations.[369]
Workers processing [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pomegranate_production_in_Afghanistan"] pomegranates
(anaar), which Afghanistan is famous
for in Asia 
 Da Afghanistan Bank serves as the central bank of the nation[370]
and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghan_afghani"] Afghani (AFN) is the national currency, with an exchange
rate of about 75 Afghanis to 1 US dollar.[371] A number of local
 and foreign banks operate in the country, including the Afghanistan
International Bank, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Kabul_Bank"] New Kabul Bank, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azizi_Bank"] Azizi Bank, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pashtany_Bank"] Pashtany Bank,
 Standard Chartered Bank, and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_MicroFinance_Bank-Afghanistan"] First Micro Finance Bank.
One of the main drivers for
the current economic recovery is the return of over 5 million
expatriates, who brought with them entrepreneurship and wealth-
creating skills as well as much needed funds to start up businesses.
Many Afghans are now involved in construction, which is one of
the largest industries in the country.[372] Some of the major national
construction projects include the $35 billion New Kabul City next
 to the capital, the Aino Mena project in Kandahar, and the Ghazi
Amanullah Khan Town near Jalalabad.[373][374][375] Similar 
 Afghan rugs are one of Afghanistan's
main exports
development projects have also begun in Herat, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mazar-e-Sharif"] Mazar-e-Sharif,
and other cities.[376] An estimated 400,000 people enter the labor market each year.[377]
Several small companies and factories began operating in different parts of the country, which not only
provide revenues to the government but also create new jobs. Improvements to the business environment
have resulted in more than $1.5 billion in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Telecommunication"] telecom investment and created more than 100,000 jobs since
2003.[378] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghan_rug"] Afghan rugs are becoming popular again, allowing many carpet dealers around the country to
hire more workers; in 2016–17 it was the fourth most exported group of items.[379]
Afghanistan is a member of WTO, SAARC, ECO, and OIC. It holds an observer status in SCO. In 2018, a
majority of imports come from either Iran, China, Pakistan and Kazakhstan, while 84% of exports are to
Pakistan and India.[380]
Since the Taliban's takeover of the country in August 2021, the United States has [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghan_frozen_assets"] frozen about $9 billion in
assets belonging to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Da_Afghanistan_Bank"] Afghan central bank,[381] blocking the Taliban from accessing billions of dollars
held in U.S. bank accounts.[382][383]
Agriculture
Agricultural production is the backbone of Afghanistan's economy[384] and has traditionally dominated the
economy, employing about 40% of the workforce as of 2018.[385] The country is known for producing
pomegranates, grapes, apricots, melons, and several other fresh and dry fruits. It is also known as the
world's largest producer of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opium_production_in_Afghanistan"] opium – as much as 16% or more of the nation's economy is derived from the
cultivation and sale of opium.[386] It is also one of the world's top producers of cannabis.[387]
Saffron, the most expensive spice, grows in Afghanistan, particularly [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herat_Province"] Herat Province. In recent years, there
has been an uptick in saffron production, which authorities and farmers trying to replace poppy cultivation.
Between 2012 and 2019, the saffron cultivated and produced in Afghanistan was consecutively ranked the
Page 27
world's  best by the International Taste and Quality
Institute.[388][389] Production hit record high in 2019 (19,469 kg of
saffron), and one kilogram is sold domestically between $634 and
$1147.[390]
The availability of cheap diesel-powered water pumps imported
from China and Pakistan, and in the 2010s, of cheap solar power to
pump water, resulted in expansion of agriculture and population in
the southwestern deserts of Afghanistan in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kandahar_Province"] Kandahar Province,
 Helmand Province and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nimruz_Province"] Nimruz Province in the 2010s. Wells have
gradually been deepened, but water resources are limited. Opium is 
Afghan [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saffron"] saffron has been recognized
as the world's best
the major crop, but as of 2022, was under attack by the new
Taliban government which, in order to suppress opium production, was systematically suppressing water
pumping.[391][392]
Mining 
The country's natural resources include: coal, copper, iron ore, lithium,
uranium, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rare_earth_element"] rare earth elements, chromite, gold, zinc, talc, barite, sulfur, lead,
marble, precious and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semi-precious_stones"] semi-precious stones, natural gas, and
petroleum.[393][394] In 2010, US and Afghan government officials
 estimated that untapped mineral deposits located in 2007 by the US
Geological Survey are worth at least $1 trillion.[395]
 Michael E. O'Hanlon of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brookings_Institution"] Brookings Institution estimated that if
Afghanistan generates about $10 billion per year from its [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mining_in_Afghanistan"] mineral deposits,
its [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gross_national_product"] gross national product would double and provide long-term funding for
 Afghan security forces and other critical needs.[396] The United States
 Lapis lazuli stones 
Geological Survey (USGS) estimated in 2006 that northern Afghanistan
has an average 460 million m3 (2.9 billion bbl) of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crude_oil"] crude oil, 440 billion m3
(15.7 trillion cu ft) of natural gas, and 67 billion L (562 million US bbl) of
 natural gas liquids.[397] In 2011, Afghanistan signed an oil exploration
contract with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China_National_Petroleum_Corporation"] China National Petroleum Corporation (CNPC) for the development of three oil fields along
the Amu Darya river in the north.[398]
The country has significant amounts of lithium, copper, gold, coal, iron ore, and other
minerals.[393][394][399] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khanashin"] Khanashin [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbonatite"] carbonatite in Helmand Province contains 1,000,000 tonnes
(980,000 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Long_ton"] long tons; 1,100,000 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Short_ton"] short tons) of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rare_earth_element"] rare earth elements.[400] In 2007, a 30-year lease was granted
for the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mes_Aynak#Copper_Mine"] Aynak copper mine to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China_Metallurgical_Group"] China Metallurgical Group for $3 billion,[401] making it the biggest
 foreign investment and private business venture in Afghanistan's history.[402] The state-run Steel Authority
of India won the mining rights to develop the huge [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hajigak_Pass"] Hajigak iron ore deposit in central Afghanistan.[403]
Government officials estimate that 30% of the country's untapped mineral deposits are worth at least
$1 trillion.[395] One official asserted that "this will become the backbone of the Afghan economy" and a
Pentagon memo stated that Afghanistan could become the "Saudi Arabia of lithium".[404] The lithium
reserves of 21 Mio. tons could amount to the ones of Bolivia, which is currently viewed as the country with
the largest lithium reserves.[405] Other larger deposits are the ones of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bauxite"] Bauxit and Cobalt.[405] In a 2011
news story, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Christian_Science_Monitor"] CSM reported, "The United States and other Western nations that have borne the brunt of
the cost of the Afghan war have been conspicuously absent from the bidding process on Afghanistan's
mineral deposits, leaving it mostly to regional powers."[406]
Page 28
Access to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biocapacity"] biocapacity in Afghanistan is lower than world average. In 2016, Afghanistan had 0.43 global
hectares[407] of biocapacity per person within its territory, much less than the world average of 1.6 global
hectares per person.[408] In 2016 Afghanistan used 0.73 global hectares of biocapacity per person - their
 ecological footprint of consumption. This means they use just under double as much biocapacity as
Afghanistan contains. As a result, Afghanistan is running a biocapacity deficit.[407]
Infrastructure
Energy
According to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Bank"] World Bank, 98% of the rural population have
access to electricity in 2018, up from 28% in 2008.[409] Overall the
figure stands at 98.7%.[410] As of 2016, Afghanistan produces
1,400 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Megawatt"] megawatts of power, but still imports the majority of
electricity via transmission lines from Iran and the Central Asian
states.[411] The majority of electricity production is via
hydropower, helped by the amount of rivers and streams that flow
from the mountains.[412] However electricity is not always reliable
and blackouts happen, including in Kabul.[413] In recent years an
increasing number of solar, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biomass"] biomass and wind power plants have
been constructed.[414] Currently under development are the 
Afghanistan electricity supply 1980–
2019
 CASA-1000 project which will transmit electricity from
 Kyrgyzstan and Tajikistan, and the Turkmenistan-Afghanistan-
Pakistan-India (TAPI) gas pipeline.[413] Power is managed by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Da_Afghanistan_Breshna_Sherkat&action=edit&redlink=1"] Da Afghanistan Breshna Sherkat
(DABS, Afghanistan Electricity Company).
Important dams include the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kajaki_Dam"] Kajaki Dam, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dahla_Dam"] Dahla Dam, and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sardeh_Band_Dam"] Sardeh Band Dam.[253]
Tourism 
Tourism is a small industry in Afghanistan due to security issues.
Nevertheless, some 20,000 foreign tourists visit the country
annually as of 2016.[415] In particular an important region for
domestic and international tourism is the picturesque [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bamyan"] Bamyan
Valley, which includes lakes, canyons and historical sites, helped
by the fact it is in a safe area away from insurgent activity.[416][417]
Smaller numbers visit and trek in regions such as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wakhan"] Wakhan
 Band-e Amir National Park 
Valley, which is also one of the world's  most remote
communities.[418] From the late 1960s onwards, Afghanistan was a
popular stop on the famous [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hippie_trail"] hippie trail, attracting many Europeans
and Americans. Coming from Iran, the trail traveled through various Afghan provinces and cities including
Herat, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kandahar"] Kandahar and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kabul"] Kabul before crossing to northern Pakistan, northern India, and Nepal.[419][420]
Tourism peaked in 1977, the year before the start of political instability and armed conflict.[421]
The city of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghazni"] Ghazni has significant history and historical sites, and together with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bamyan"] Bamyan city have in recent
years been voted Islamic Cultural Capital and South Asia Cultural Capital respectively.[422] The cities of
Herat, Kandahar, Balkh, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zaranj"] Zaranj are also very historic. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minaret_of_Jam"] Minaret of Jam in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hari_River,_Afghanistan"] Hari River valley is a
 UNESCO World Heritage Site. A cloak reputedly worn by Islam's prophet [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad"] Muhammad is kept inside the
 Shrine of the Cloak in Kandahar, a city founded by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_the_Great"] Alexander the Great and the first capital of
Page 29
Afghanistan. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Citadel_of_Alexander"] citadel of Alexander in the western city of Herat has been
renovated in recent years and is a popular attraction. In the north of the
country is the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shrine_of_Ali"] Shrine of Ali, believed by many to be the location where [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali"] Ali
was buried.[423] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Museum_of_Afghanistan"] National Museum of Afghanistan is located in Kabul
and hosts a large number of Buddhist, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bactria"] Bactrian Greek and early Islamic
antiquities; the museum suffered greatly by civil war but has been slowly
restoring since the early 2000s.[424]
Communication
 Telecommunication services in Afghanistan are provided by Afghan
Telecom, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghan_Wireless"] Afghan Wireless, Etisalat, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MTN_Group"] MTN Group, and Roshan. The
country uses its own space [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Satellite"] satellite called [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghansat_1"] Afghansat 1, which provides
services to millions of phone, internet, and television subscribers. By 2001
following years of civil war, telecommunications was virtually a non-
existent sector, but by 2016 it had grown to a $2 billion industry, with
22 million mobile phone subscribers and 5 million internet users. The sector
employs at least 120,000 people nationwide.[425] 
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minaret_of_Jam"] Minaret of Jam is a
 UNESCO World Heritage
Site, currently under threat
by erosion and flooding
Transportation 
Due to Afghanistan's geography, transport between various parts of
the country has historically been difficult. The backbone of
Afghanistan's road network is [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Highway_1_(Afghanistan)"] Highway 1, often called the "Ring
Road",  which extends for 2,210 kilometers (1,370 mi) and
connects five major cities: Kabul, Ghazni, Kandahar, Herat and
Mazar-i-Sharif,[426] with spurs to Kunduz and Jalalabad and
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salang_Tunnel"] Salang Tunnel, once the highest 
various border crossings, while skirting around the mountains of
the Hindu Kush.[427]
tunnel in the world, provides a key
connection between the north and
south of the country 
The Ring Road is crucially important for domestic and international
trade and the economy.[428] A key portion of the Ring Road is the
 Salang Tunnel, completed in 1964, which facilitates travel through
the Hindu Kush mountain range and connects northern and
 southern Afghanistan.[429] It is the only land route that connects Central Asia to the Indian
subcontinent.[430] Several mountain passes allow travel between the Hindu Kush in other areas. Serious
traffic accidents are common on Afghan roads and highways, particularly on the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kabul%E2%80%93Kandahar_Highway"] Kabul–Kandahar and the
 Kabul–Jalalabad Road.[431] Traveling by bus in Afghanistan remains dangerous due to militant
activities.[432]
Air transport in Afghanistan is provided by the national carrier, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ariana_Afghan_Airlines"] Ariana Afghan Airlines,[433] and by the
private company [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kam_Air"] Kam Air. Airlines from a number of countries also provide flights in and out of the
country. These include [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Air_India"] Air India, Emirates, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_Air"] Gulf Air, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran_Aseman_Airlines"] Iran Aseman Airlines, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan_International_Airlines"] Pakistan International Airlines,
and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Airlines"] Turkish Airlines. The country has four international airports: [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamid_Karzai_International_Airport"] Hamid Karzai International Airport
(formerly Kabul International Airport), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kandahar_International_Airport"] Kandahar International Airport, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herat_International_Airport"] Herat International Airport, and
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mazar-e_Sharif_International_Airport"] Mazar-e Sharif International Airport. Including domestic airports, there are 43.[10] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bagram_Air_Base"] Bagram Air Base is a
major military airfield.
Page 30
The country has three rail links: one, a 75-kilometer (47 mi) line
from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mazar-i-Sharif"] Mazar-i-Sharif to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghanistan%E2%80%93Uzbekistan_Friendship_Bridge"] Uzbekistan border;[434] a 10-kilometer
(6.2 mi) long line from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toraghundi"] Toraghundi to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkmenistan"] Turkmenistan border
(where it continues as part of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkmen_Railways"] Turkmen Railways); and a short link
from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aqina"] Aqina across the Turkmen border to Kerki, which is planned
to be extended further across Afghanistan.[435] These lines are used
for freight only and there is no passenger service. A rail line
between Khaf, Iran and Herat, western Afghanistan, intended for
both freight and passengers, is under construction as of
2019.[436][437] About 125 kilometers (78 mi) of the line will lie on
the Afghan side.[438][439] There are various proposals for the
construction of additional rail lines in the country.[440] 
 An Ariana Afghan Airlines Airbus
A310 in 2006
Private vehicle ownership has increased substantially since the early 2000s. Taxis are yellow in color and
consist of both cars and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auto_rickshaw"] auto rickshaws.[441] In rural Afghanistan, villagers often use donkeys, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mule"] mules or
 horses to transport or carry goods. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camel"] Camels are primarily used by the Kochi nomads.[265] Bicycles are
popular throughout Afghanistan.[442]
Culture
 Afghans have both common cultural features and those that differ
between the regions of Afghanistan, each with distinctive cultures
partly as a result of geographic obstacles that divide the
country.[249] Family is the mainstay of Afghan society and families
are often headed by a patriarch.[443] In the southern and eastern
region, the people live according to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pashtun_culture"] Pashtun culture by
following [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pashtunwali"] Pashtunwali (the Pashtun way).[444] Key tenets of
Pashtunwali include hospitality, the provision of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nanawatai"] sanctuary to those
seeking refuge, and revenge for the shedding of blood.[445] The
Pashtuns are largely connected to the culture of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Asia"] Central Asia and
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Plateau"] Iranian Plateau. The remaining Afghans are culturally [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persianization"] Persian
and Turkic. Some non-Pashtuns who live in proximity with 
An Afghan family near Kholm, 1939
– most Afghans are tribal
Pashtuns have adopted Pashtunwali in a  process called
Pashtunization, while some Pashtuns have been Persianized. Those who have lived in Pakistan and Iran
over the last 30 years have been further influenced by the cultures of those neighboring nations. The
Afghan people are known to be strongly religious.[286]
Afghans, particularly Pashtuns, are noted for their tribal solidarity and high regard for personal honor.[446]
One writer considers the tribal system to be the best way of organizing large groups of people in a country
that is geographically difficult, and in a society that, from a materialistic point of view, has an
uncomplicated lifestyle.[447] There are various [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Afghanistan"] Afghan tribes, and an estimated 2–3 million nomads.[448]
Afghan culture is deeply Islamic,[449] but pre-Islamic practices persist.[450] One example is [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bacha_bazi"] bacha bazi, a
term for activities involving sexual relations between older men and younger adolescent men, or boys.[451]
 Child marriage is prevalent in Afghanistan;[452] the legal age for marriage is 16.[453] The most preferred
 marriage in Afghan society is to one's parallel cousin, and the groom is often expected to pay a bride
price.[454]
In the villages, families typically occupy [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mudbrick"] mudbrick houses, or compounds with mudbrick or [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stone_wall"] stone walled
houses. Villages typically have a headman (malik), a master for water distribution (mirab) and a religious
teacher (mullah). Men would typically work on the fields, joined by women during harvest.[443] About
Page 31
15% of the population are nomadic, locally called [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kochi_people"] kochis.[249]
When nomads pass villages they often buy supplies such as tea,
wheat and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kerosene"] kerosene from the villagers; villagers buy [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wool"] wool and milk
from the nomads.[443]
 Afghan clothing for both men and women typically consists of
various forms of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shalwar_kameez"] shalwar kameez, especially [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perahan_tunban"] perahan tunban and
 khet partug.  Women would normally wear a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chador"] chador for head
covering; some women, typically from highly conservative
communities, wear the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Burqa"] burqa, a full body covering. These were
worn by some women of the Pashtun community well before Islam
came to the region, but the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taliban"] Taliban enforced this dress on women
when they were in power.[455] Another popular dress is the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chapan"] chapan 
A house occupied by nomadic kochi
people in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nangarhar_Province"] Nangarhar Province
which acts as a coat. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karakul_(hat)"] karakul is a hat made from the fur of a specific regional breed of sheep. It was
favored by former kings of Afghanistan and became known to much of the world in the 21st century when
it was constantly worn by President [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamid_Karzai"] Hamid Karzai.[456] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakol"] pakol is another traditional hat originating
from the far east of the country; it was popularly worn by the guerrilla leader [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmad_Shah_Massoud"] Ahmad Shah Massoud.[457]
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mazari_hat"] Mazari hat originates from northern Afghanistan.[458]
Architecture
The nation has a complex history that has survived either in
its current cultures or in the form of various languages and
monuments. Afghanistan contains many remnants from all
ages, including [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greece"] Greek and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddhist"] Buddhist stupas, monasteries,
monuments, temples and Islamic minarets. Among the most
 well known are the Great Mosque of Herat, the Blue
Mosque, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minaret_of_Jam"] Minaret of Jam, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chil_Zena"] Chil Zena, the Qala-i Bost
in Lashkargah, the ancient Greek city of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ai-Khanoum"] Ai-Khanoum.[459]
However, many of its historic monuments have been
damaged in modern times due to the civil wars.[460] The two 
Kabul skyline, displaying both historical and
contemporary buildings
famous [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddhas_of_Bamiyan"] Buddhas of Bamiyan were destroyed by the Taliban,
who regarded them as idolatrous. Despite that, archaeologists are still finding Buddhist relics in different
parts of the country, some of them dating back to the 2nd century.[461] As there was no colonialism in the
modern era in Afghanistan, European-style architecture is rare but does exist: the Victory Arch at [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paghman"] Paghman
and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Darul_Aman_Palace"] Darul Aman Palace in Kabul were built in this style in the 1920s by the Afghans themselves.
Art and ceramics
A traditional Afghan [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Embroidery"] embroidery
pattern 
Carpet [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weaving"] weaving is an ancient practice in Afghanistan, and many of
these are still [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Handicraft"] handmade by tribal and nomadic people today.[298]
Carpets have been produced in the region for thousands of years
and traditionally done by women.[462] Some crafters express their
feelings through the designs of rugs; for example after the outbreak
of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Afghan_War"] Soviet–Afghan War, "[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_rugs"] war rugs", a variant of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghan_rug"] Afghan rugs,
were created with designs representing pain and misery caused by
the conflict.[463] Every province has its own specific characteristics
in making rugs.[464] In some of the Turkic-populated areas in the
north-west, bride and wedding ceremony prices are driven by the
bride's weaving skills.[465]
Page 32
 Pottery has been crafted in Afghanistan for millennia. The village of Istalif, north of Kabul, is in particular a
major center, known for its unique turquoise and green pottery,[466] and their methods of crafting have
remained the same for centuries.[467][468] Much of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lapis_lazuli"] lapis lazuli stones were earthed in modern-day
Afghanistan which were used in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_porcelain"] Chinese porcelain as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cobalt_blue"] cobalt blue, later used in ancient [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesopotamia"] Mesopotamia and
Turkey.[469]
The lands of Afghanistan have a long history of art, with the world's earliest known usage of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oil_painting"] oil painting
found in cave murals in the country.[470][471] A notable art style that developed in Afghanistan and eastern
Pakistan is [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gandhara_Art"] Gandhara Art, produced by a fusion of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greco-Roman"] Greco-Roman art and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddhist_art"] Buddhist art between the 1st and
7th centuries CE.[472] Later eras saw increased use of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_miniature"] Persian miniature style, with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kamaleddin_Behzad"] Kamaleddin Behzad
of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herat"] Herat being one of the most notable miniature artists of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timurid_dynasty"] Timurid and early [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Safavid"] Safavid periods. Since the
1900s, the nation began to use Western techniques in art. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdul_Ghafoor_Breshna"] Abdul Ghafoor Breshna was a prominent Afghan
painter and sketch artist from Kabul during the 20th century.
Media and entertainment
 Afghanistan has around 350 radio stations and over 200 television stations.[473] Radio Television
Afghanistan, originating from 1925, is the state public broadcaster. Television programs began airing in the
1970s and today there are many private television channels such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TOLO_(TV_channel)"] TOLO and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shamshad_TV"] Shamshad TV. The first
Afghan newspaper was published in 1873,[474] and there are hundreds of print outlets today.[473] By the
 1920s, Radio Kabul was broadcasting local radio services.[475] Voice of America, BBC, and Radio Free
Europe/Radio Liberty (RFE/RL) broadcast in both of Afghanistan's official languages on radio.[476] Press
restrictions have been gradually relaxed and private media diversified since 2002, after more than two
decades of tight controls.
Afghans have long been accustomed to watching Indian [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bollywood"] Bollywood films and listening to its [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Filmi"] filmi
songs.[477] It has been claimed that Afghanistan is among the biggest markets for the Hindi film
industry.[478] The stereotypes of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghans_in_India"] Afghans in India (Kabuliwala or Pathani) have also been represented in
some Bollywood films by actors.[479] Many Bollywood film stars have roots in Afghanistan, including
 Salman Khan, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saif_Ali_Khan"] Saif Ali Khan, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aamir_Khan"] Aamir Khan, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feroz_Khan_(Indian_actor)"] Feroz Khan, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kader_Khan"] Kader Khan, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naseeruddin_Shah"] Naseeruddin Shah, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zarine_Khan"] Zarine Khan,
 Celina Jaitly, and a number of others. Several Bollywood films have been shot inside Afghanistan,
including [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dharmatma"] Dharmatma, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khuda_Gawah"] Khuda Gawah, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Escape_from_Taliban"] Escape from Taliban, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kabul_Express"] Kabul Express.
Music
 Afghan classical music has close historical links with Indian
classical music and use the same Hindustani terminology and
theories like raga. Genres of this style of music include [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghazal"] ghazal
(poetic music) and instruments such as the Indian tabla, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sitar"] sitar and
harmonium, and local instruments like zerbaghali, as well as
 dayereh and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tanbur"] tanbur which are also known in Central Asia, the
Caucusus and the Middle East. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rubab_(instrument)"] rubab is the country's national
instrument and precurses the Indian [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sarod"] sarod instrument. Some of the
famous artists of classical music include [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ustad_Sarahang"] Ustad Sarahang and
Sarban.[480] 
The Afghan [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rubab_(instrument)"] rubab
Pop music developed in the 1950s through [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radio_Kabul"] Radio Kabul and was influential in social change. During this
time female artists also started appearing, at first [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mermon_Parwin"] Mermon Parwin.[480] Perhaps the most famous artist of
this genre was [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmad_Zahir"] Ahmad Zahir, who synthesized many genres and continues to be renowned for his voice
Page 33
and rich lyrics long after his death in 1979.[481][480] Other notable masters of traditional or popular Afghan
music include Nashenas, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ubaidullah_Jan"] Ubaidullah Jan, Mahwash, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmad_Wali"] Ahmad Wali, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Farhad_Darya"] Farhad Darya, and Naghma.[482]
 Attan is the national dance of Afghanistan, a group dance popularly performed by Afghans of all
backgrounds.[483] The dance is considered part of Afghan identity.[484]
Cuisine
Afghan cuisine is largely based upon the nation's chief crops, such
as wheat, maize, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barley"] barley and rice. Accompanying these staples are
native fruits and vegetables as well as dairy products such as milk,
 yogurt and whey. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kabuli_palaw"] Kabuli palaw is the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_dish"] national dish of
Afghanistan.[485] The nation's culinary specialties reflect its ethnic
and geographic diversity.[486] Afghanistan is known for its high
quality pomegranates, grapes, and sweet melons.[487] Tea is a
favorite drink among Afghans, and a typical diet consists of naan,
yoghurts, rice and meat.[443]
Literature 
 Non (bread) from a local baker, the
most widely consumed bread in
Afghanistan
Classic [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_literature"] Persian and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pashto_poetry"] Pashto poetry are a cherished part of Afghan culture. Poetry has always been one of the
major educational pillars in the region, to the level that it has integrated itself into culture.[488] One of the
poetic styles is called landay. A popular theme in Afghan folklore and mythology are Divs, monstrous
creatures.[489] Thursdays are traditionally "poetry night" in the city of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herat"] Herat when men, women and
children gather and recite both ancient and modern poems.[490]
The Afghan region has produced countless Persian-speaking poets and writers from the Middle Ages to the
present day, among which three mystical authors are considered true national glories (although claimed
with equal ardor by Iran), namely: [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khwaja_Abdullah_Ansari"] Khwaja Abdullah Ansari of Herat, a great mystic and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sufi"] Sufi saint in the
11th century, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanai"] Sanai of Ghazni, author of mystical poems in the 12th century, and, finally, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rumi"] Rumi of Balkh, in
the 13th century, considered the persophonist throughout the world as the greatest mystical poet of the
entire Muslim world. The Afghan Pashto literature, although quantitatively remarkable and in great growth
in the last century, has always had an essentially local meaning and importance, feeling the influence of
both Persian literature and the contiguous literatures of India. Both main literatures, from the second half of
the nineteenth century, have shown themselves to be sensitive to genres (novel, theater), movements and
stylistic features imported from Europe.
 Khushal Khan Khattak of the 17th century is considered the national poet. Other notable poets include
 Rabi'a Balkhi, Jami, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rahman_Baba"] Rahman Baba, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khalilullah_Khalili"] Khalilullah Khalili, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parween_Pazhwak"] Parween Pazhwak.[491]
Holidays and festivals
Afghanistan's official New Year starts with Nowruz, an ancient tradition that started as a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zoroastrian"] Zoroastrian
celebration in present-day Iran, and with which it shares the annual celebration along with several other
countries. It occurs every year at the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/March_equinox"] vernal equinox. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nauruz_in_Afghanistan"] In Afghanistan, Nowruz is typically celebrated with
music and dance, as well as holding [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buzkashi"] buzkashi tournaments.[492]
Page 34
Yaldā, another nationally celebrated ancient tradition,[493]
commemorates the ancient goddess [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mithra"] Mithra and marks the longest
night of the year on the eve of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winter_solstice"] winter solstice (čelle ye
zemestān; usually falling on 20 or 21 December),[494][495] during
which families gather together to recite poetry and eat fruits—
particularly the red fruits watermelon and pomegranate, as well as
 mixed nuts.[496][497]
Religious festivals are also celebrated; as a predominantly Muslim
country, Islamic events and festivals such as Ramadan, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eid_al-Fitr"] Eid al-Fitr
and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashura"] Ashura are widely celebrated annually in Afghanistan. The
Sikh festival of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vaisakhi"] Vaisakhi is celebrated by the Sikh community[498]
and the Hindu festival [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diwali"] Diwali by the Hindu community.[499]
 National Independence Day is celebrated on 19 August to mark the
 Anglo-Afghan Treaty of 1919 under King [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amanullah_Khan"] Amanullah Khan and
the country's  full independence.[500] Several international Haft Mewa (Seven Fruit Syrup) is
celebrations are also officially held in Afghanistan, such as  popularly consumed during Nowruz in
 International Workers' Day and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Women%27s_Day"] International Women's Day. Some Afghanistan
regional festivals include the Pamir Festival, which celebrates the
culture of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wakhi_people"] Wakhi and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kyrgyz_people"] Kyrgyz peoples, the Red Flower Festival
(during Nowruz) in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mazar-i-Sharif"] Mazar-i-Sharif and the Damboora Festival in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bamyan_Province"] Bamyan Province.
Sports
Sport in Afghanistan is managed by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghan_Sports_Federation"] Afghan Sports Federation.
 Cricket and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Association_football"] Association football are the two most popular sports in
the country.[501][502] The Afghan Sports Federation promotes
cricket, association football, basketball, volleyball, golf, handball,
boxing, taekwondo, weightlifting, bodybuilding, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Track_and_field"] track and field,
skating, bowling, snooker, chess, and other sports.
Afghanistan's sports teams are increasingly celebrating titles at
international events. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghanistan_national_basketball_team"] basketball team won the first team sports title
at the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010_South_Asian_Games"] 2010 South Asian Games.[503] Later that year, the country's 
The ancient national sport of
Afghanistan, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buzkashi"] Buzkashi
 cricket team followed it with the winning of 2009–10 ICC
 Intercontinental Cup.[504] In 2012, the country's 3x3 basketball team won the gold medal at the 2012 Asian
Beach Games. In 2013, Afghanistan's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghanistan_national_football_team"] football team followed as it won the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SAFF_Championship"] SAFF Championship.[505]
 The Afghan national cricket team, which was formed in 2001, participated in the 2009 ICC World Cup
Qualifier, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010_ICC_World_Cricket_League_Division_One"] 2010 ICC World Cricket League Division One and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010_ICC_World_Twenty20"] 2010 ICC World Twenty20. It won the
 ACC Twenty20 Cup in 2007, 2009, 2011 and 2013. The team eventually made it and played in the 2015
Cricket World Cup.[506] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghanistan_Cricket_Board"] Afghanistan Cricket Board (ACB) is the official governing body of the sport
and is headquartered in Kabul. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alokozay_Kabul_International_Cricket_Ground"] Alokozay Kabul International Cricket Ground serves as the nation's
 main cricket stadium. There are several other stadiums throughout the country, including the Ghazi
Amanullah Khan International Cricket Stadium near Jalalabad. Domestically, cricket is played between
teams from different provinces.
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghanistan_national_football_team"] Afghanistan national football team has been competing in international [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Association_football"] football since 1941.[507] The
national team plays its home games at the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghazi_Stadium"] Ghazi Stadium in Kabul, while [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Football_in_Afghanistan"] football in Afghanistan is
governed by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghanistan_Football_Federation"] Afghanistan Football Federation. The national team has never competed or qualified for
Page 35
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup"] FIFA World Cup but has recently won an international football trophy in 2013.[505] The country also
has a national team in the sport of futsal, a 5-a-side variation of football.
The traditional and the national sport of Afghanistan is buzkashi, mainly popular in the north, but also
having a following in other parts of the country.[508] It is similar to polo, played by horsemen in two teams,
each trying to grab and hold a goat carcass.[509] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghan_Hound"] Afghan Hound (a type of running dog) originated in
Afghanistan and was formerly used in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wolf_hunting_with_dogs"] wolf hunting. In 2002, traveler [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rory_Stewart"] Rory Stewart reported that dogs were
still used for wolf hunting in remote areas.[510]

37. 
"The name Afghan has evidently been derived from Asvakan, the Assakenoi of Arrian... "
(Megasthenes and Arrian, p 180. See also: Alexander's Invasion of India, p 38; J.W.
McCrindle).
"Even the name Afghan is Aryan being derived from Asvakayana, an important clan of
the Asvakas or horsemen who must have derived this title from their handling of
celebrated breeds of horses" (See: Imprints of Indian Thought and Culture Abroad, p
124, Vivekananda Kendra Prakashan).
cf: "Their name (Afghan) means "cavalier" being derived from the Sanskrit, Asva, or
Asvaka, a horse, and shows that their country must have been noted in ancient times, as
it is at the present day, for its superior breed of horses. Asvaka was an important tribe
settled north to Kabul river, which offered a gallant resistance but ineffectual resistance
to the arms of Alexander "(Ref: Scottish Geographical Magazine, 1999, p 275, Royal
Scottish Geographical Society).
"Afghans are Assakani of the Greeks; this word being the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanskrit"] Sanskrit [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashvaka"] Ashvaka meaning
'horsemen'" (Ref: Sva, 1915, p 113, Christopher Molesworth Birdwood).
Cf: "The name represents Sanskrit Asvaka in the sense of a cavalier, and this reappears
scarcely modified in the Assakani or Assakeni of the historians of the expedition of
Alexander" (Hobson-Jobson: A Glossary of Colloquial [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anglo-Indian"] Anglo-Indian words and phrases,
and of kindred terms, etymological..by Henry Yule, AD Burnell).

140. [URL: "https://books.google.com/books?id=I2chrSJCW54C&pg=PA129"] Klass, Rosanne (1994). The Widening Circle of Genocide (https://books.google.com/books?
id=I2chrSJCW54C&pg=PA129). Transaction Publishers. p. 129. ISBN 978-[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-4128-3965-5"] 1-4128-3965-5.
"During the intervening fourteen years of Communist rule, an estimated 1.5 to 2 million
Afghan civilians were killed by Soviet forces and their proxies- the four Communist regimes
in Kabul, and the East Germans, Bulgarians, Czechs, Cubans, Palestinians, Indians and
others who assisted them. These were not battle casualties or the unavoidable civilian
victims of warfare. Soviet and local Communist forces seldom attacked the scattered guerilla
bands of the Afghan Resistance except, in a few strategic locales like the Panjsher valley.
Instead they deliberately targeted the civilian population, primarily in the rural areas."

widely reported accounts, substantial programmes of depopulation have been conducted in
these Afghan provinces: Ghazni, Nagarhar, Lagham, Qandahar, Zabul, Badakhshan,
Lowgar, Paktia, Paktika and Kunar...There is considerable evidence that genocide has been
committed against the Afghan people by the combined forces of the Democratic Republic of
Afghanistan and the Soviet Union."
